World Flower Guide — All Flower Species

A comprehensive guide to all flower species in the world, covering origins, colors, families and descriptions.

Home

All Flower Species of the World

This guide covers 1,712 flowering plant species found across the world. Each entry includes the common name, scientific name, family, origin, and a description of the species. Click any flower name to read the full profile.

Sunflower (Helianthus annuus), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. The sunflower is a vibrant and iconic plant, instantly recognizable for its large, daisy-like flower head. Native to North America, it's cultivated for its seeds and oil. Their heliotropic nature, turning to face the sun, is a remarkable characteristic.

Tulip (Tulipa), from the Liliaceae family, is native to Central Asia. Tulips are beloved for their vibrant colors and simple, elegant form, making them a quintessential spring flower. Originating from the mountainous regions of Central Asia, they were introduced to Europe in the 16th century. Today, they are cultivated worldwide in a vast array of cultivars.

Daffodil (Narcissus), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa. The daffodil, also known as narcissus, is a cheerful harbinger of spring with its distinctive trumpet-shaped corona. Native to meadows and woods in Europe and North Africa, they are among the first flowers to bloom. Their bright yellow and white colors symbolize hope and joy.

Lily (Lilium), from the Liliaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Lilies are stately and elegant flowers, often prized for their large, showy petals and intoxicating fragrance. Found across the Northern Hemisphere, they have been cultivated for thousands of years. Their trumpet, bowl, or star-shaped flowers come in a multitude of colors.

Orchid (Orchidaceae), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Worldwide (except Antarctica). Orchids are a vast and incredibly diverse family of flowering plants, renowned for their complex and often strikingly beautiful blooms. They are found on every continent except Antarctica, thriving in a wide range of habitats. Their intricate structures and long-lasting flowers have captivated botanists and enthusiasts for centuries.

Peony (Paeonia), from the Paeoniaceae family, is native to Asia, Europe, North America. Peonies are beloved for their abundant, often fragrant, and exquisitely layered flowers that bloom in late spring. Native to Asia, Europe, and North America, these perennial plants produce large, showy blossoms. They are a symbol of romance, prosperity, and good fortune.

Hydrangea (Hydrangea), from the Hydrangeaceae family, is native to Asia, Americas. Hydrangeas are popular shrubs known for their large, spherical clusters of flowers that can change color based on soil acidity. Originating from Asia and the Americas, these plants thrive in dappled shade. The color of their blooms, ranging from blues and purples to pinks and whites, is a fascinating natural phenomenon.

Carnation (Dianthus caryophyllus), from the Caryophyllaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Carnations are hardy, long-blooming flowers with distinctive ruffled petals and a unique, spicy fragrance. Native to the Mediterranean region, they have been cultivated for over two millennia. Their wide range of colors and long vase life make them a popular choice for bouquets and arrangements.

Marigold (Tagetes), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Americas. Marigolds are vibrant and prolific bloomers, known for their sunny shades of yellow, orange, and red. Originating from the Americas, these annuals are a staple in many gardens. Beyond their aesthetic appeal, they are also valued for their natural pest-repelling qualities.

Petunia (Petunia), from the Solanaceae family, is native to South America. Petunias are beloved for their abundant, trumpet-shaped flowers that bloom continuously throughout the summer months. Native to South America, these popular annuals come in a dazzling array of colors. They are perfect for adding a splash of vibrant, long-lasting color to hanging baskets and garden beds.

Geranium (Pelargonium), from the Geraniaceae family, is native to South Africa. Geraniums, technically pelargoniums, are popular garden plants known for their bright, cheerful flowers and often attractive foliage. Originating from South Africa, they are widely cultivated for their ease of care and continuous bloom. They add a touch of classic beauty to containers, window boxes, and garden beds.

Lavender (Lavandula), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Lavender is an aromatic herb and flowering plant celebrated for its soothing fragrance and beautiful purple spikes. Native to the Mediterranean region, it thrives in sunny, well-drained conditions. Its essential oil is widely used in aromatherapy, perfumes, and culinary applications.

Begonia (Begonia), from the Begoniaceae family, is native to South and Central America, Africa, Asia. Begonias are a diverse group of plants appreciated for both their attractive foliage and their colorful, often elaborate, flowers. Found in tropical and subtropical regions across the globe, they are well-suited for shady garden spots. Their varied forms, from wax begonias to rhizomatous varieties, offer a wide range of beauty.

Dahlia (Dahlia), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mexico and Central America. Dahlias are renowned for their spectacular and highly varied floral forms, ranging from simple single petals to complex pom-poms and spiky cactus types. Native to Mexico and Central America, these tuberous perennials produce an astonishing spectrum of colors. They are a celebrated choice for late-summer and autumn gardens.

Iris (Iris), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. The iris is an elegant flower characterized by its unique structure of three upright petals (standards) and three hanging sepals (falls). Found widely across the Northern Hemisphere, these rhizomatous or bulbous plants bloom in a rich palette of colors. They are often associated with royalty and admiration.

Zinnia (Zinnia), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Zinnias are cheerful, easy-to-grow annuals celebrated for their vibrant, long-lasting blooms and their ability to attract butterflies. Native to North America, they come in a wide range of colors and flower forms. These sturdy plants are a favorite for cutting gardens and border plantings.

Chrysanthemum (Chrysanthemum), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Asia, Northeastern Europe. Chrysanthemums, often called 'mums', are a quintessential autumn flower, gracing gardens with their diverse shapes and vibrant colors as the season wanes. Originating from Asia and Northeastern Europe, these plants offer a spectacular display before frost. They symbolize longevity and joy in many cultures.

Cosmos (Cosmos), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mexico, Central America, South America. Cosmos are delicate, airy flowers with daisy-like petals that add a touch of ethereal beauty to the garden. Native to the Americas, these annuals are known for their long blooming period and graceful movement in the wind. They are excellent for naturalizing and attracting pollinators.

Aster (Aster), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Worldwide (except Antarctica). Asters are charming, star-shaped flowers that provide a burst of color to gardens in late summer and fall. Found across much of the globe, these perennials are a vital food source for pollinators heading into winter. Their name, derived from the Greek word for 'star,' perfectly describes their radiant appearance.

Freesia (Freesia), from the Iridaceae family, is native to South Africa. Freesias are exquisite cormous perennials celebrated for their intensely fragrant, trumpet-shaped flowers and graceful arching stems. Native to South Africa, they are a popular choice for cut flowers due to their long vase life and delightful aroma. Their vibrant colors add a cheerful touch to arrangements.

Gladiolus (Gladiolus), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Africa, Mediterranean. Gladioli are striking plants known for their tall, upright flower spikes adorned with large, showy blooms. Originating from Africa and the Mediterranean, these cormous perennials symbolize strength and integrity. Their dramatic presence makes them a focal point in gardens and a popular choice for floral arrangements.

Hyacinth (Hyacinthus), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Eastern Mediterranean. Hyacinths are highly fragrant spring-blooming bulbs, producing dense spikes of bell-shaped flowers. Native to the Eastern Mediterranean region, they are cherished for their powerful, sweet perfume and vibrant colors. They are a classic component of spring bulb displays.

Delphinium (Delphinium), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Delphiniums are majestic plants renowned for their tall, stately spikes of richly colored flowers, often in brilliant shades of blue and purple. Native to the Northern Hemisphere, they add vertical interest and drama to garden borders. Their graceful blooms are a favorite for cottage gardens and formal designs.

Anemone (Anemone), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Worldwide (except Antarctica). Anemones are charming, delicate flowers known for their cup-shaped blooms, often featuring a contrasting dark center. Found worldwide, these perennial plants offer a variety of bloom times and colors, from early spring to autumn. They add a touch of whimsical beauty to garden beds and rockeries.

Crocus (Crocus), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Middle East. Crocuses are among the earliest harbingers of spring, their small, goblet-shaped flowers often pushing through residual snow. Native to Europe, North Africa, and the Middle East, these cormous perennials announce the end of winter. Their vibrant colors bring a welcome cheer to the landscape.

Ranunculus (Ranunculus), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Mediterranean, Western Asia. Ranunculus flowers are renowned for their incredibly dense, papery petals, creating exquisite, rose-like blooms. Originating from the Mediterranean and Western Asia, these tubers produce a stunning display of vibrant colors. They are a favorite for bouquets and adding a touch of elegance to gardens.

Lisianthus (Eustoma), from the Gentianaceae family, is native to North America, South America. Lisianthus are elegant flowers often compared to roses due to their layered petals and sophisticated appearance. Native to North and South America, they offer a delicate beauty and come in a range of soft colors. Their long vase life makes them a popular choice for floristry.

Sweet Pea (Lathyrus odoratus), from the Fabaceae family, is native to Italy. Sweet peas are cherished for their intoxicating fragrance and delicate, butterfly-shaped blooms that adorn climbing vines. Native to Italy, these annuals are a beloved addition to gardens and floral arrangements. Their sweet scent and ethereal beauty evoke a sense of nostalgia and charm.

Calla Lily (Zantedeschia), from the Araceae family, is native to South Africa. Calla lilies are distinguished by their unique, trumpet-shaped spathes that gracefully unfurl. Native to South Africa, these rhizomatous plants bring an air of sophisticated elegance to any setting. Their sleek lines and various colors make them a popular choice for both gardens and floral designs.

Gerbera Daisy (Gerbera jamesonii), from the Asteraceae family, is native to South Africa. Gerbera daisies are undeniably cheerful, known for their large, vibrant flower heads that resemble classic daisies. Native to South Africa, these popular plants bring a burst of sunny disposition to gardens and arrangements. Their wide array of bright colors is sure to lift any mood.

Lobelia (Lobelia), from the Campanulaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Lobelia is a genus of flowering plants known for their small, often intensely colored blooms, frequently in shades of blue and purple. Found globally, many species are used ornamentally, particularly for their ability to cascade from hanging baskets and containers. They add delicate beauty and striking color to garden edges.

Impatiens (Impatiens), from the Balsaminaceae family, is native to Tropical and Southern Africa, Madagascar, Southeast Asia. Impatiens are a favorite for shady gardens, offering a profusion of colorful blooms that persist throughout the season. Originating from tropical regions, these popular annuals thrive in cooler, moist conditions. They provide a reliable splash of vibrant color where other flowers might struggle.

Begonia Tuberous (Begonia x tuberhybrida), from the Begoniaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Tuberous begonias are prized for their exceptionally large and showy flowers, often featuring ruffled or camellia-like forms. Developed as hybrids, they are known for their spectacular color range and dramatic presence. These plants are perfect for adding a luxurious touch to shaded patios and gardens.

Cyclamen (Cyclamen), from the Primulaceae family, is native to Mediterranean, Southwest Asia, Central Europe. Cyclamen are charming plants recognized by their delicate, nodding flowers with uniquely swept-back petals and attractive, often patterned, foliage. Native to the Mediterranean and surrounding regions, they bloom in a variety of soft colors. They are popular as houseplants and in cooler climates, as garden bedding plants.

Fuchsia (Fuchsia), from the Onagraceae family, is native to Central and South America, New Zealand, Tahiti. Fuchsias are enchanting plants featuring distinctive, pendulous flowers that resemble tiny, colorful skirts or dancers. Native to the Americas and Oceania, they are often grown in hanging baskets where their graceful blooms can be fully appreciated. Their vibrant, bi-colored petals create a unique visual appeal.

Portulaca (Portulaca), from the Portulacaceae family, is native to South America. Portulaca, also known as moss rose, is a vibrant, low-growing annual renowned for its cheerful, cup-shaped flowers that open in direct sunlight. Native to South America, it thrives in hot, dry conditions and sandy soils. These resilient plants provide a continuous carpet of bright color throughout the summer.

Lobularia maritima (Lobularia maritima), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Sweet alyssum is a low-growing annual prized for its masses of tiny, fragrant white flowers that create a carpet of delicate blooms. Native to the Mediterranean, it thrives in full sun and well-drained soil. This versatile plant is perfect for edging beds, spilling over containers, and attracting beneficial insects.

Celosia (Celosia), from the Amaranthaceae family, is native to Tropical regions. Celosia offers uniquely textured and vibrantly colored flowers, available in dramatic crested ('cockscomb') and feathery plumed forms. Originating from tropical regions, these annuals add a bold, exotic touch to gardens and floral arrangements. Their striking appearance makes them a standout choice for visual impact.

Vinca (Catharanthus roseus), from the Apocynaceae family, is native to Madagascar. Periwinkle, or Vinca, is a remarkably tough and reliable annual prized for its glossy foliage and profusion of cheerful flowers. Native to Madagascar, it thrives in heat and humidity, making it an excellent choice for summer bedding. Its consistent bloom makes it a popular landscaping plant.

Salvia (Salvia), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Salvia, commonly known as sage, is a diverse genus of flowering plants featuring tall spikes of often brilliantly colored flowers. Found globally, many varieties are excellent for attracting bees and butterflies to the garden. Their architectural form and vibrant hues make them a popular choice for borders and beds.

Echinacea (Echinacea), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Echinacea, or coneflower, is a beloved native prairie flower characterized by its distinctive cone-shaped center and swept-back petals. Originating from North America, it is also recognized for its reputed immune-boosting properties. These hardy perennials provide long-lasting color and attract pollinators.

Gaillardia (Gaillardia), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Gaillardia, commonly called blanket flower, boasts daisy-like blooms with striking bicolor petals in fiery shades of red and yellow. Native to North America, these resilient perennials thrive in hot, dry conditions. They are a favorite for attracting butterflies and adding a splash of intense color to the landscape.

Coreopsis (Coreopsis), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Americas. Coreopsis, often called tickseed, is a cheerful perennial that produces abundant, bright yellow daisy-like flowers over a long season. Native to the Americas, these hardy plants are known for their drought tolerance and ease of care. They bring a sunny disposition to borders and meadows.

Achillea (Achillea millefolium), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, North America. Yarrow, scientifically known as Achillea, features flat-topped clusters of tiny flowers that are a favorite of beneficial insects. Native to Europe, Asia, and North America, this hardy perennial is also valued for its fern-like foliage and historical medicinal uses. Its sturdy nature makes it suitable for challenging garden conditions.

Hemerocallis (Hemerocallis), from the Asphodelaceae family, is native to Asia. Daylilies, belonging to the genus Hemerocallis, are incredibly popular for their prolific blooming and wide range of colors. Originating from Asia, each flower typically lasts only one day, but the plant produces a continuous succession of buds. They are highly adaptable and low-maintenance garden staples.

Aquilegia (Aquilegia), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Columbine, scientifically Aquilegia, is admired for its unique and intricate spurred flowers that resemble tiny fairy bonnets. Native to the Northern Hemisphere, these woodland perennials add a delicate charm to shaded gardens. Their unusual form and diverse color palette make them a captivating addition.

Digitalis (Digitalis purpurea), from the Plantaginaceae family, is native to Europe, Northwest Africa, Southwest Asia. Foxgloves, or Digitalis, are stately plants known for their impressive spires of tubular flowers, often spotted within. Native to Europe and surrounding regions, they are a classic cottage garden plant that attracts bumblebees. Their dramatic vertical presence adds architectural interest to the landscape.

Pansy (Viola x wittrockiana), from the Violaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Pansies are beloved cool-season annuals, instantly recognizable by their distinctive 'face'-like markings and velvety petals. Developed as hybrids, they offer a wide array of vibrant colors and patterns. They are perfect for early spring and fall gardens, adding a cheerful splash of color.

Viola (Viola), from the Violaceae family, is native to Worldwide (mostly Northern Hemisphere). The genus Viola encompasses a wide variety of small, often charmingly fragrant flowers, most famously the violet. Found primarily in the Northern Hemisphere, these delicate blooms are a symbol of modesty and faithfulness. They are perfect for naturalizing in lawns or adding a touch of subtle beauty to shaded areas.

Bellis perennis (Bellis perennis), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe. The common or English daisy, Bellis perennis, is a low-growing perennial that forms a rosette of leaves topped with charming, simple flower heads. Native to Europe, it is often found in lawns and meadows, adding a touch of natural cheer. Its compact size and cheerful blooms make it a delightful addition to garden edges.

Thymus (Thymus vulgaris), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Thyme is a wonderfully aromatic herb that produces clusters of tiny, delicate flowers, often in shades of pink or purple. Native to the Mediterranean, it is a popular choice for groundcover and culinary use. Its resilience and fragrant foliage make it a valuable addition to herb gardens and rockeries.

Sempervivum (Sempervivum), from the Crassulaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Iran. Sempervivum, commonly known as 'hens and chicks,' are remarkably resilient succulents that form tight, attractive rosettes. Native to Europe, North Africa, and Iran, these drought-tolerant plants are perfect for rock gardens and containers. They reproduce by sending out smaller offsets, or 'chicks', from the mother plant ('hen').

Sedum (Sedum), from the Crassulaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Sedums are a diverse group of hardy succulents, many of which produce clusters of star-shaped flowers, often in vibrant pinks, reds, or yellows. Found throughout the Northern Hemisphere, these drought-tolerant plants are excellent for rock gardens and difficult sites. Many varieties bloom in late summer and fall, providing color when other plants fade.

Echeveria (Echeveria), from the Crassulaceae family, is native to Mexico, Central America, South America. Echeverias are popular succulents renowned for their beautifully sculpted, fleshy leaves that form perfect geometric rosettes. Native to the Americas, these drought-tolerant plants come in a stunning array of colors and textures. They are ideal for containers, rock gardens, and creating miniature succulent landscapes.

Hosta (Hosta), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to East Asia. Hostas are prized primarily for their stunning foliage, offering a vast diversity of leaf colors, textures, and sizes that thrive in shady conditions. Native to East Asia, these herbaceous perennials also produce attractive spikes of bell-shaped flowers, typically in shades of white or lavender. They are a cornerstone of shade gardens.

Astilbe (Astilbe), from the Saxifragaceae family, is native to Asia, Europe. Astilbe are elegant perennials known for their feathery, plume-like flower clusters that add graceful texture and color to shady garden areas. Native to Asia and Europe, they prefer moist soil and partial shade. Their upright blooms provide a soft, romantic feel to the landscape.

Heuchera (Heuchera), from the Saxifragaceae family, is native to North America. Heucheras, commonly called coral bells, are primarily grown for their exceptionally colorful and diverse foliage, ranging from deep burgundy to vibrant lime green. Native to North America, they also produce delicate, airy spikes of small bell-shaped flowers. They are an excellent choice for adding texture and color to borders and containers.

Ligularia (Ligularia), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Ligularias are striking plants featuring large, bold foliage and tall spikes of bright yellow or orange, daisy-like flowers. Native to Europe and Asia, they thrive in moist, shady conditions. Their dramatic presence makes them a focal point in the woodland or bog garden.

Rodgersia (Rodgersia), from the Saxifragaceae family, is native to East Asia. Rodgersia plants are impressive for their large, textured, palmate leaves and their stately plumes of frothy white or pink flowers. Native to East Asia, they prefer moist, shady environments, similar to hostas. They bring a bold, architectural element to the garden.

Dicentra (Dicentra spectabilis), from the Papaveraceae family, is native to East Asia. Bleeding hearts, scientifically Dicentra spectabilis, are iconic spring-blooming perennials featuring uniquely shaped flowers that resemble dangling hearts. Native to East Asia, they prefer cool, moist, shady conditions. Their delicate charm and distinctive form make them a beloved garden plant.

Pulmonaria (Pulmonaria), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Europe, Russia. Pulmonaria, commonly known as lungwort, is a delightful shade-loving perennial recognized for its attractive, often silver-spotted foliage and clusters of bell-shaped flowers that change color. Native to Europe and Russia, they bloom early in the spring. Their unique foliage adds interest to the garden even after flowering.

Brunnera (Brunnera macrophylla), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Siberia, the Caucasus. Brunnera macrophylla, also called Siberian bugloss, is a shade-loving perennial valued for its beautiful heart-shaped leaves, often with silver variegation. Native to Siberia and the Caucasus, it produces delicate clusters of small, true-blue, forget-me-not-like flowers in spring. It provides excellent groundcover and textural interest.

Galium odoratum (Galium odoratum), from the Rubiaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Asia Minor. Sweet woodruff, Galium odoratum, is a delightful, low-growing groundcover known for its fragrant foliage and clusters of small, star-shaped white flowers. Native to Europe and surrounding regions, it thrives in shady, moist conditions. Its sweet scent is often used in potpourri and culinary applications.

Helleborus (Helleborus), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Hellebores, often called Lenten roses or Christmas roses, are highly prized for their ability to bloom in the depths of winter. Native to Europe and Asia, these evergreen perennials produce nodding flowers in a wide array of colors, including whites, pinks, purples, and even near-blacks. They bring welcome color to the garden when little else is in bloom.

Hepatica (Hepatica), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Hepatica are charming, small woodland wildflowers that emerge early in spring, often before the leaves fully unfurl. Native to the Northern Hemisphere, they are characterized by their distinctive lobed leaves and delicate, cup-shaped flowers. These ephemeral plants bring a touch of exquisite beauty to the forest floor.

Jeffersonia diphylla (Jeffersonia diphylla), from the Berberidaceae family, is native to Eastern North America. Twinleaf, or Jeffersonia diphylla, is a rare and beautiful native woodland perennial notable for its distinctive double-lobed leaves that resemble two leaves joined together. Originating from eastern North America, it produces solitary, pure white flowers in early spring. This plant adds an element of botanical curiosity to shady gardens.

Trillium (Trillium), from the Melanthiaceae family, is native to North America. Trilliums are iconic native woodland wildflowers, characterized by their distinctive three leaves arranged in a whorl, topped by a single, striking flower. Found primarily in North America, these slow-growing plants are a symbol of pristine forest ecosystems. Their elegant simplicity is highly admired.

Cypripedium (Cypripedium), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Lady's slipper orchids, belonging to the genus Cypripedium, are captivating native orchids distinguished by their unique, pouched petals that resemble a slipper. Found across the Northern Hemisphere, these woodland beauties are highly sought after for their intricate and unusual floral structures. They are a treasure of native flora.

Phlox (Phlox), from the Polemoniaceae family, is native to North and Central America. Phlox are popular flowering plants offering a spectrum of colors and forms, from tall, fragrant garden phlox to low-growing, creeping varieties. Native to North and Central America, they are known for their clusters of star-shaped flowers that attract pollinators. They provide vibrant color and delightful fragrance to gardens.

Monarda (Monarda), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to North America. Bee balm, scientifically Monarda, is an aromatic native plant that produces spectacular whorls of tubular flowers, highly attractive to bees, butterflies, and hummingbirds. Originating from North America, it is a favorite for wildlife gardens and borders. Its fragrant foliage also adds to its appeal.

Agastache (Agastache), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to North America, Asia. Agastache, often called hyssop or hummingbird mint, is an aromatic plant known for its attractive spikes of tubular flowers and fragrant foliage. Native to North America and Asia, it is a magnet for pollinators, particularly hummingbirds. Its upright form and long bloom time make it a valuable addition to sunny gardens.

Lupine (Lupinus), from the Fabaceae family, is native to Americas, Mediterranean. Lupines are striking plants renowned for their tall, elegant spires of pea-like flowers, creating dramatic vertical accents in the garden. Native to the Americas and the Mediterranean region, they come in a wide array of vibrant colors. These nitrogen-fixing plants are both beautiful and beneficial to the soil.

Penstemon (Penstemon), from the Plantaginaceae family, is native to North America. Penstemons, commonly known as beardtongues, are a diverse group of native perennials featuring tubular flowers that are a favorite of hummingbirds and bees. Originating from North America, they offer a spectacular range of colors and bloom times. Their upright growth habit adds structure to borders.

Asclepias (Asclepias tuberosa), from the Apocynaceae family, is native to North America. Butterfly weed, Asclepias tuberosa, is a vital native perennial celebrated for its brilliant clusters of orange flowers, which are crucial for monarch butterfly caterpillars. Originating from North America, it thrives in sunny, well-drained conditions. This plant is a cornerstone of pollinator gardens.

Anigozanthos (Anigozanthos), from the Haemodoraceae family, is native to Southwestern Australia. Kangaroo paws, scientifically Anigozanthos, are unique Australian wildflowers named for their striking, fuzzy flower stalks that resemble a kangaroo's paw. Native to southwestern Australia, they are drought-tolerant and produce spectacular blooms in a range of vibrant colors. They add an exotic touch to gardens in suitable climates.

Leucospermum (Leucospermum), from the Proteaceae family, is native to South Africa. Pincushion flowers, belonging to the genus Leucospermum, are spectacular South African natives renowned for their intricate, vibrant blooms that resemble pincushions. These proteas offer a unique texture and stunning display of color, often in fiery oranges and reds. They are a focal point in fynbos gardens and floral arrangements.

Banksia (Banksia), from the Proteaceae family, is native to Australia. Banksias are iconic Australian plants, instantly recognizable by their unique, cylindrical flower spikes that attract a wide array of wildlife. Native to Australia, these shrubs and trees offer a remarkable range of flower colors and forms. They are a vital part of the Australian landscape and a striking addition to gardens in appropriate climates.

Protea (Protea), from the Proteaceae family, is native to South Africa. Proteas, including the majestic King Protea, are South African natives celebrated for their large, bold, and unique flower heads. They are symbolic of change and courage, and their striking appearance makes them a popular choice for floral arrangements. These plants are adapted to arid conditions and unique soil types.

Strelitzia (Strelitzia reginae), from the Strelitziaceae family, is native to South Africa. The bird of paradise, Strelitzia reginae, is a dramatic tropical plant known for its spectacular, crane-like flowers in vibrant oranges and blues. Native to South Africa, it brings a touch of exotic flair to gardens and is a popular cut flower. Its unique form and bold colors make it instantly recognizable.

Callistemon (Callistemon), from the Myrtaceae family, is native to Australia. Bottlebrush plants, scientifically Callistemon, are recognizable by their cylindrical flower spikes that resemble brushes used for cleaning bottles. Native to Australia, they are known for their vibrant colors, often in shades of red, and their ability to attract nectar-feeding birds. These attractive shrubs add a unique visual element to gardens.

Grevillea (Grevillea), from the Proteaceae family, is native to Australia. Grevilleas are a diverse genus of Australian plants known for their unique, spider-like flowers that are rich in nectar, making them a favorite of nectar-feeding birds. Native to Australia, they come in a wide array of forms and vibrant colors, from deep reds to bright yellows. These hardy plants are well-adapted to Australian conditions.

Brunsvigia (Brunsvigia josephinae), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to South Africa. Brunsvigia josephinae, commonly known as Josephine's lily or candelabra lily, is a spectacular bulbous plant producing a massive, umbrella-shaped inflorescence of numerous pink to red flowers. Native to South Africa, it is one of the largest of the amaryllis family. Its dramatic floral display is a sight to behold when it blooms.

Crassula (Crassula ovata), from the Crassulaceae family, is native to South Africa. The jade plant, Crassula ovata, is a popular succulent known for its thick, fleshy leaves and tree-like habit. Native to South Africa, it is prized as a houseplant and can produce clusters of small, star-shaped white or pink flowers, especially when mature. It is often associated with good luck and prosperity.

Kalanchoe (Kalanchoe blossfeldiana), from the Crassulaceae family, is native to Madagascar. Kalanchoe blossfeldiana, often called flaming Katy or widow's thrill, is a popular succulent plant known for its long-lasting clusters of brightly colored flowers. Native to Madagascar, it is frequently given as a gift for its vibrant display. These compact plants offer cheerful color for extended periods.

Graptopetalum (Graptopetalum), from the Crassulaceae family, is native to Mexico. Graptopetalum are attractive succulents that form dense rosettes of fleshy leaves, often with a powdery coating. Native to Mexico, they are known for their delicate, star-shaped flowers, typically white or pale yellow, that bloom in spring. These easy-to-care-for plants are popular for succulent arrangements.

Echeveria 'Lola' (Echeveria 'Lola'), from the Crassulaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Echeveria 'Lola' is a highly sought-after hybrid known for its stunning pastel coloration, featuring powdery pink and blue-grey leaves forming a perfect rosette. This cultivar is a favorite among succulent enthusiasts for its elegant appearance. It produces delicate pinkish flowers during its blooming season.

Haworthia (Haworthia), from the Asphodelaceae family, is native to South Africa. Haworthias are small, architectural succulents native to South Africa, prized for their unique foliage patterns, often featuring translucent 'windows' or raised white tubercles. While not showy bloomers, they produce delicate, often white or greenish flowers on tall stalks. They are ideal for small pots and terrariums.

Aloe (Aloe vera), from the Asphodelaceae family, is native to Arabian Peninsula. The aloe plant, most famously Aloe vera, is a succulent renowned for its medicinal properties derived from its thick, fleshy leaves. Native to the Arabian Peninsula, it is also cultivated for its striking architectural form. It produces tall spikes of often yellowish or orange tubular flowers when mature.

Agave (Agave), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Americas. Agaves are dramatic succulents known for their large, spiky rosettes of thick, fleshy leaves, often in shades of blue-green or grey. Native to the Americas, they are famous for their monocarpic nature, producing a spectacular flower stalk once in their lifetime before dying. Their architectural form makes them a statement plant in arid gardens.

Yucca (Yucca), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Americas. Yuccas are striking plants characterized by their stiff, sword-like leaves forming a rosette, topped by tall spikes of bell-shaped white or cream flowers. Native to the Americas, they are well-adapted to arid conditions. Their sculptural form and impressive blooms add a dramatic element to dry gardens and landscapes.

Opuntia (Opuntia), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Americas. Prickly pear cacti, belonging to the genus Opuntia, are distinctive succulents with flat, paddle-like stem segments covered in glochids and spines. Native to the Americas, they are known for producing showy, colorful flowers, often in vibrant yellows, oranges, and pinks. They are a classic symbol of desert landscapes.

Cereus (Cereus), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Americas. Cereus cacti are large, columnar desert plants, many of which are famous for their spectacular, often fragrant, night-blooming flowers. Native to the Americas, their impressive size and architectural form make them prominent features in desert gardens. The fleeting beauty of their nocturnal blooms is a marvel.

Lophophora (Lophophora williamsii), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Mexico, USA (Texas). The peyote cactus, Lophophora williamsii, is a small, spineless cactus native to Mexico and southern Texas. It is known for its distinctive ribbed surface and its infrequent, small, pink or white flowers that bloom at the top. This cactus holds significant cultural and spiritual importance in certain indigenous traditions.

Ariocarpus (Ariocarpus), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Mexico, USA (Texas). Ariocarpus, often called living rock cacti, are incredibly slow-growing succulents that mimic the appearance of textured rocks, providing excellent camouflage. Native to Mexico and southern Texas, they produce beautiful, solitary flowers, usually in shades of white, pink, or yellow, at the apex of the plant. Their unique form is a testament to adaptation.

Mammillaria (Mammillaria), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Mexico, Central America, Caribbean. Mammillaria are a large genus of small, globular or cylindrical cacti, easily identified by their numerous tubercles (fleshy projections) arranged in spirals. Native to Mexico and surrounding regions, they are known for producing abundant, often brightly colored flowers, typically in rings around the top of the plant. They are popular among cactus collectors for their diversity and ease of care.

Rebutia (Rebutia), from the Cactaceae family, is native to South America (Andes). Rebutias are small, clustering cacti native to the high Andes of South America, prized for their prolific and vibrant flowers. They often form dense clumps and produce an abundance of colorful blooms that emerge from near the apex of the stems. Their compact size and spectacular flowering make them a favorite for collectors.

Gymnocalycium (Gymnocalycium), from the Cactaceae family, is native to South America. Gymnocalycium, commonly known as chin cactus, are globular or flattened cacti native to South America, characterized by their prominent ribs and attractive, often large flowers. The flowers typically emerge from areoles along the ribs and come in a range of vibrant colors. These popular cacti are appreciated for their unique shapes and beautiful blooms.

Epiphyllum (Epiphyllum), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Mexico, Central and South America. Epiphyllums, also known as orchid cacti, are epiphytic cacti native to the Americas, meaning they grow on other plants. They are celebrated for their large, spectacular, and often highly fragrant flowers that bloom nocturnally or diurnally depending on the species. Their flattened, leaf-like stems are quite unique among cacti.

Schlumbergera (Schlumbergera), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Brazil. Schlumbergera species, commonly known as Christmas cactus or Thanksgiving cactus, are popular epiphytic cacti native to Brazil. They are renowned for their festive blooming season, typically around the winter holidays, producing an abundance of vibrant, segmented flowers. These easy-to-care-for houseplants bring cheerful color indoors.

Rhipsalis (Rhipsalis), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Americas, Africa, Madagascar. Rhipsalis, often referred to as mistletoe cacti, are a genus of epiphytic cacti known for their trailing, often segmented stems. Native to the Americas, Africa, and Madagascar, they produce small, delicate flowers, typically in shades of white or cream, followed by small berries. Their pendulous growth habit makes them excellent for hanging baskets.

Hoya (Hoya), from the Apocynaceae family, is native to Australia, Asia. Hoyas, commonly called wax plants, are popular vining houseplants known for their thick, fleshy leaves and their clusters of star-shaped, waxy flowers. Originating from Australia and Asia, these tropical plants produce incredibly fragrant blooms. Their unique texture and sweet scent make them a favorite among plant enthusiasts.

Dischidia (Dischidia), from the Apocynaceae family, is native to Australia, Asia. Dischidia are a genus of climbing or trailing epiphytes, closely related to Hoyas, native to Australia and Asia. They are known for their unique adaptations, such as modified, hollow leaves that can host ant colonies. While their flowers are typically small and inconspicuous, their unusual foliage and trailing habit are highly ornamental.

Hibiscus (Hibiscus rosa-sinensis), from the Malvaceae family, is native to Tropical Asia. Native to tropical Asia, it is a quintessential symbol of the tropics. These ornamental shrubs are a favorite for their bold, exotic beauty and long flowering season.

Brugmansia (Brugmansia), from the Solanaceae family, is native to South America. These blooms are highly fragrant, especially at night, and come in a range of colors. The plant is toxic and should be handled with care.

Datura (Datura), from the Solanaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Datura, often called Jimsonweed, are herbaceous plants known for their large, trumpet-shaped flowers, which are often fragrant and bloom at night. Found worldwide, these plants are distinctive in appearance but are highly toxic. Their dramatic blooms are a notable feature in gardens where they can be cultivated.

Nicotiana (Nicotiana), from the Solanaceae family, is native to Americas. Native to the Americas, they add a unique scent and delicate beauty to gardens. While the common tobacco plant is well-known, many ornamental species are cultivated for their blooms.

Species vary in color, offering yellow, orange, green, purple, and white blooms. Their intoxicating scent makes them a captivating addition to gardens, especially for evening enjoyment.

Brunfelsia (Brunfelsia), from the Solanaceae family, is native to Tropical Americas. Typically starting as purple, they mature to lavender and finally to white, creating a multi-hued display. Their sweet fragrance adds to their charm.

Lavender (Lavandula angustifolia), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Lavender is a fragrant flowering plant beloved for its soothing scent and beautiful purple spikes. Native to the Mediterranean region, it has been used for centuries in perfumes, aromatherapy, and culinary applications. Its resilience and low maintenance make it a garden favorite.

Lilac (Syringa vulgaris), from the Oleaceae family, is native to Southeastern Europe to Eastern Asia. Lilacs are deciduous shrubs celebrated for their intensely fragrant, conical clusters of flowers. Native to southeastern Europe and parts of Asia, their intoxicating scent is synonymous with spring. They are cherished for their beautiful blooms and ability to evoke fond memories.

Carnivorous Pitcher Plant (Nepenthes), from the Nepenthaceae family, is native to Southeast Asia. Pitcher plants are carnivorous plants with specialized leaves modified into pitfall traps that capture insects. Native to Southeast Asia, these fascinating plants use nectar to lure prey into their digestive fluids. Their unique adaptations make them a subject of great botanical interest.

Venus Flytrap (Dionaea muscipula), from the Droseraceae family, is native to North Carolina, USA. The Venus Flytrap is a famous carnivorous plant known for its rapid snap-trap mechanism that captures prey. Native to a small region of North and South Carolina, its leaves are equipped with sensitive trigger hairs. When disturbed, the lobes rapidly close, trapping insects inside.

Sundew (Drosera), from the Droseraceae family, is native to Worldwide. Sundews are a diverse genus of carnivorous plants that capture insects using sticky glands on their leaves. Found worldwide, their leaves are covered in glistening tentacles that resemble dewdrops, hence their name. These sticky traps effectively immobilize and digest their prey.

Butterwort (Pinguicula), from the Lentibulariaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Butterworts are carnivorous plants with leaves that are covered in tiny glands producing a sticky secretion. Found on every continent except Antarctica, they use this 'sticky trap' to catch small insects like gnats and fruit flies. Many species also produce attractive, often violet or pink, flowers.

Water Lily (Nymphaea), from the Nymphaeaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Water lilies are aquatic flowering plants with large, round floating leaves and beautiful, often fragrant flowers. Found in calm waters worldwide, their blooms typically open during the day and close at night. They are symbols of purity and beauty in many cultures.

Lotus (Nelumbo nucifera), from the Nelumbonaceae family, is native to Asia, Australia. The Lotus is a sacred aquatic plant revered for its beauty and symbolism of purity and enlightenment. Native to Asia and Australia, its large, striking pink or white flowers emerge majestically from muddy waters. The seed pods are also distinctive and often used in floral arrangements.

Bromeliad (Bromeliaceae), from the Bromeliaceae family, is native to Americas. Bromeliads are a diverse family of tropical plants, many of which are epiphytic, growing on other plants. Native to the Americas, they are known for their striking, architectural rosettes of leaves and vibrant, often colorful, floral spikes. Many species collect water in their central cups.

Air Plant (Tillandsia) (Tillandsia), from the Bromeliaceae family, is native to Americas. Air plants are fascinating epiphytic plants belonging to the Bromeliad family, requiring no soil. Native to the Americas, they absorb water and nutrients directly from the air through specialized scales on their leaves. Many produce beautiful, colorful, and delicate flowers.

Cypress (Cupressus), from the Cupressaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Cypress trees are evergreen conifers characterized by their aromatic foliage, typically scale-like or awl-shaped. Arborvitae (Thuja), from the Cupressaceae family, is native to North America, East Asia. Juniper (Juniperus), from the Cupressaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Junipers are hardy evergreen conifers with diverse forms, from groundcovers to large trees. Native to the Northern Hemisphere, their foliage is typically needle-like or scale-like, and they produce fleshy, berry-like cones. They are prized for their drought tolerance and adaptability.

Spruce (Picea), from the Pinaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Native to the Northern Hemisphere, they are widely recognized for their pyramidal shape and are popular for Christmas trees and timber. Their dense foliage provides year-round structure.

Pine (Pinus), from the Pinaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Pines are well-known coniferous evergreen trees characterized by their needles, which grow in bundles. Native to the Northern Hemisphere, they are recognized by their distinctive cones and are valuable for timber, paper, and resin. Their needles provide year-round green interest in the landscape.

Fir (Abies), from the Pinaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Firs are coniferous evergreen trees known for their soft, flat needles and upright cones that disintegrate on the tree. Native to the Northern Hemisphere, they are popular for their symmetrical form and pleasant fragrance. Their dense foliage makes them a staple in forests and landscapes.

Cedar (Cedrus), from the Pinaceae family, is native to Mediterranean, Himalayas. True Cedars are large coniferous evergreen trees native to the Mediterranean and Himalayas. They are characterized by their short, needle-like foliage that grows in clusters or whorls on woody spurs. Cedars are often majestic trees with a distinctive scent and significant cultural importance.

Douglas Fir (Pseudotsuga menziesii), from the Pinaceae family, is native to Western North America. Douglas Fir is a towering coniferous evergreen native to western North America. It is recognized by its soft, flat needles and distinctive cones with prominent three-pronged bracts. This species is a vital source of timber and a popular Christmas tree.

Bald Cypress (Taxodium distichum), from the Cupressaceae family, is native to Southeastern USA. The Bald Cypress is a unique deciduous conifer native to the southeastern United States, notable for its feathery, soft needles that turn a beautiful russet-red in autumn. It thrives in wet conditions and often develops characteristic 'knees' projecting from the soil. Its transformation in fall is a striking seasonal event.

Ginkgo (Ginkgo biloba), from the Ginkgoaceae family, is native to China. The Ginkgo is considered a 'living fossil,' being the sole surviving species of an ancient order. Native to China, it is distinctive for its unique fan-shaped leaves that turn a brilliant golden-yellow in the fall. This hardy tree is also known for its resilience and medicinal properties.

Forget-Me-Not (Myosotis sylvatica), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. These delicate flowers are known for their charming, small blue petals. They thrive in shady, moist environments, often found in woodlands and along stream banks. Their name, forget-me-not, carries a romantic symbolism of enduring memory.

Daffodil (Narcissus pseudonarcissus), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa. Daffodils are cheerful spring bulbs characterized by their distinctive trumpet-shaped corona. They are one of the first flowers to bloom, pushing through the soil as winter recedes. Their vibrant yellow hues are a welcome sign of warmer days ahead.

Tulip (Tulipa gesneriana), from the Liliaceae family, is native to Central Asia. Tulips are iconic spring-blooming bulbs prized for their elegant, cup-shaped flowers. Originating from Central Asia, they have been cultivated for centuries and are now grown worldwide. Their smooth, waxy petals come in almost every color imaginable.

Iris (Iris germanica), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Europe, Mediterranean. The iris is a sophisticated flower with unique, intricate petal structures. It is characterized by its three upright 'standards' and three hanging 'falls,' often featuring a fuzzy beard. 'Germanica' is a common variety, admired for its regal appearance.

Peony (Paeonia lactiflora), from the Paeoniaceae family, is native to China. Peonies are prized for their large, opulent flowers that boast many layers of soft petals. They are long-lived perennials, often passed down through generations. Their romantic, full blooms make them a garden favorite.

Geranium (Pelargonium x hortorum), from the Geraniaceae family, is native to Southern Africa. Commonly known as 'zonal geraniums,' these plants are popular for their vibrant clusters of flowers. They are hardy and adaptable, thriving in sunny spots. Their foliage often has distinctive concentric rings.

Begonia (Begonia semperflorens), from the Begoniaceae family, is native to South America. Wax begonias are reliable bloomers, producing masses of small, waxy flowers throughout the season. They tolerate partial shade and are excellent for borders and containers. Their glossy foliage adds to their appeal.

Marigold (Tagetes erecta), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mexico. Marigolds are cheerful and resilient flowers, known for their bright yellow and orange blooms. They are often planted in vegetable gardens as they are believed to deter certain pests. Their prolific flowering provides continuous color.

Salvia (Salvia splendens), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Brazil. Salvias are known for their striking flower spikes that attract a variety of pollinators. Many varieties offer vibrant colors like red, blue, and purple. They are generally low-maintenance and bloom prolifically.

Fuchsia (Fuchsia magellanica), from the Onagraceae family, is native to South America. Fuchsias are captivating plants with unique, pendulous flowers that resemble tiny dancers. They come in a wide range of color combinations, often featuring vibrant pinks, purples, and reds. These plants prefer partial shade and consistent moisture.

Hosta (Hosta plantaginea), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to East Asia. Hostas are primarily grown for their beautiful, varied foliage, but they also produce attractive flower spikes. The flowers are typically bell-shaped and often fragrant, appearing in summer. They thrive in shady, moist garden conditions.

Hydrangea (Hydrangea macrophylla), from the Hydrangeaceae family, is native to Japan. Hydrangeas are famous for their spectacular, large flower clusters that can be globe-shaped or flattened. The color of the blooms can often change depending on the soil's pH. They are striking shrubs that offer significant visual impact.

Wisteria (Wisteria sinensis), from the Fabaceae family, is native to China. Wisteria is a vigorous climbing vine known for its breathtaking cascades of fragrant, pea-like flowers. These blooms typically appear in spring, creating a spectacular display of color. The plant requires strong support due to its rapid growth.

Camellia (Camellia japonica), from the Theaceae family, is native to Japan, China, Korea. Camellias are exquisite flowering shrubs known for their beautiful, rose-like blooms. They typically flower in the cooler months, offering color when many other plants are dormant. Their glossy, dark green leaves provide an attractive backdrop.

Rhododendron (Rhododendron ponticum), from the Ericaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Rhododendrons are renowned for their large, spectacular flower trusses, often blooming in vibrant colors. They are evergreen shrubs that prefer acidic soil and dappled shade. These plants are a cornerstone of many woodland gardens.

Heather (Calluna vulgaris), from the Ericaceae family, is native to Europe. Heather, also known as Scotch heather, is a low-growing shrub covered in tiny, bell-shaped flowers. It blooms in late summer and autumn, creating a beautiful carpet of color. This resilient plant thrives in exposed, acidic conditions.

Bluebell (Hyacinthoides non-scripta), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Western Europe. Their delicate, bell-like blossoms are a truly enchanting sight.

Snowdrop (Galanthus nivalis), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to Europe, Middle East. Snowdrops are among the first flowers to bloom, often pushing through snow in late winter. Their delicate, nodding white flowers are a welcome sign of approaching spring. These small bulbs are a symbol of hope and resilience.

Crocus (Crocus vernus), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Middle East. Crocuses are cheerful spring bulbs that emerge from the ground with their goblet-shaped flowers. They are among the first signs of life after winter, often blooming in early spring. Their vibrant colors add a welcome splash to awakening landscapes.

Anemone (Anemone coronaria), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Anemones are known for their vibrant, cup-shaped flowers, often featuring a contrasting dark central eye. They bloom in spring and come in a wide range of striking colors. These flowers add a touch of delicate beauty to gardens.

Delphinium (Delphinium elatum), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe, North America, Asia. Delphiniums are renowned for their impressive flower spikes, which can reach several feet in height. They are particularly famous for their stunning shades of blue and purple. These tall perennials are a majestic addition to any garden.

Poppy (Papaver rhoeas), from the Papaveraceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Asia. Poppies are known for their delicate, papery petals and often vibrant colors. They can range from the iconic bright red corn poppy to softer hues. Many varieties have a striking dark central 'eye'.

Ranunculus (Ranunculus asiaticus), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Eastern Mediterranean. Ranunculus flowers are breathtakingly beautiful, featuring tightly packed layers of delicate petals that resemble roses. They come in a wide spectrum of jewel tones and pastels. These blooms are highly prized for their intricate beauty.

Aster (Aster amellus), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Asters are beloved fall-blooming perennials that offer a burst of color when many other plants are winding down. Their daisy-like flowers provide a beautiful display in shades of purple, pink, and white. They are attractive to late-season pollinators.

Chrysanthemum (Chrysanthemum x morifolium), from the Asteraceae family, is native to China. Chrysanthemums, often called 'mums,' are iconic fall flowers known for their abundant and diverse blooms. Dahlia (Dahlia pinnata), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mexico. From delicate cactus-like petals to giant dinner-plate blooms, they are a gardener's delight. These tubers produce spectacular flowers throughout summer and fall.

Gladiolus (Gladiolus communis), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Africa, Mediterranean. Gladioli are striking cut flowers known for their tall, sword-like stems and dramatic, funnel-shaped blossoms that open progressively up the spike. They come in a vast range of vibrant colors and are popular for adding vertical interest to gardens and arrangements. These cormous perennials require well-drained soil.

Chrysanthemum (Chrysanthemum indicum), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Asia. Chrysanthemum indicum is a species of chrysanthemum known for its prolific blooming and association with autumn. Dianthus (Dianthus barbatus), from the Caryophyllaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Freesia (Freesia refracta), from the Iridaceae family, is native to South Africa. Ranunculus (Ranunculus ficaria), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Western Asia. Tiarella (Tiarella cordifolia), from the Saxifragaceae family, is native to Eastern North America. Hibiscus (Hibiscus syriacus), from the Malvaceae family, is native to Asia. Datura (Datura stramonium), from the Solanaceae family, is native to Likely Americas. Nicotiana (Nicotiana alata), from the Solanaceae family, is native to South America. Anise Hyssop (Agastache foeniculum), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to North America. Anise hyssop is a fragrant perennial herb with a distinct anise scent and spikes of purple-blue flowers. It is a favorite of bees, butterflies, and hummingbirds, making it an excellent addition to pollinator gardens. This hardy plant thrives in full sun and is also used for its edible flowers and leaves.

Mignonette (Reseda odorata), from the Resedaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Mignonette is an old-fashioned annual plant celebrated for its intensely sweet and unique fragrance, despite its unassuming appearance. Its small, greenish-white to yellowish flowers emit a captivating scent. This plant is often grown for its perfume and adds a subtle charm to gardens.

Wallflower (Erysimum), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, North Africa. Wallflowers are a group of flowering plants known for their often fragrant, colorful blooms that can appear in a variety of shades. Many species are biennial or perennial, providing color in both spring and fall. They are often found growing in rocky crevices, hence their name.

Candytuft (Iberis sempervirens), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Candytuft is a low-growing, evergreen perennial that produces masses of white, umbrella-shaped flowers in spring. Its dense foliage and profuse blooms make it an excellent choice for ground cover, rock gardens, and borders. This plant adds a delightful splash of pure white to the landscape.

Creeping Thyme (Thymus serpyllum), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa. Creeping thyme is a low-growing, mat-forming groundcover prized for its fragrant foliage and delicate pink to purple flowers. It's perfect for planting between stepping stones, in rock gardens, or as a lawn substitute. The plant releases a pleasant aroma when stepped on.

Aubrieta (Aubrieta), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Aubrieta is a charming rock garden plant that forms cascading mounds of small, vibrant flowers in shades of purple, pink, and blue. It blooms profusely in spring, creating a stunning display over stone walls and rockeries. This hardy perennial adds a splash of intense color to dry, sunny locations.

Rock Cress (Arabis caucasica), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Rock cress is a hardy, low-growing perennial that forms a dense mat of silvery-grey foliage. In spring, it erupts in a profusion of small white or pink flowers, creating a lovely carpet. It's ideal for rock gardens, walls, and borders where it can spread and cascade.

Edelweiss (Leontopodium alpinum), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe (Alps). Edelweiss is an iconic alpine flower native to the mountains of Europe, particularly the Alps. It is recognized by its distinctive, fuzzy white bracts that surround the true flowers, giving it a star-like appearance. This hardy plant is adapted to harsh, high-altitude conditions.

Alpine Aster (Aster alpinus), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Alpine aster is a delightful compact perennial that thrives in alpine and rock garden settings. It produces striking daisy-like flowers, most commonly in shades of purple and blue, with bright yellow centers. These flowers appear in late spring and early summer, adding vibrant color to mountainous or rocky landscapes.

Morning Glory (Ipomoea purpurea), from the Convolvulaceae family, is native to Tropical Americas. Morning glories are fast-growing annual vines famous for their trumpet-shaped flowers that open with the morning sun and close in the afternoon. They offer a vibrant display of color in shades of blue, purple, pink, and white. These climbers are ideal for covering trellises, fences, and arbors.

Poinsettia (Euphorbia pulcherrima), from the Euphorbiaceae family, is native to Mexico. The poinsettia is an iconic plant associated with the Christmas season, famed for its vibrant, colorful bracts that surround the true flowers. Native to Mexico, its distinctive appearance has made it a global holiday symbol. While the colorful parts are not true petals, they create a spectacular display.

Christmas Rose (Helleborus niger), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe. The Christmas rose is a hardy perennial that blooms in the heart of winter, offering delicate white flowers when little else is in bloom. Its sturdy blossoms provide a welcome splash of color during the coldest months. This plant is a true treasure for its unique blooming period.

Winter Jasmine (Jasminum nudiflorum), from the Oleaceae family, is native to China. Winter jasmine is a deciduous shrub that brightens the winter landscape with its cheerful, bright yellow flowers. Blooming on bare stems before the leaves emerge, it provides a welcome splash of color during the coldest months. This adaptable plant can be grown as a sprawling shrub or trained on a support.

Winter Aconite (Eranthis hyemalis), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe. Winter aconite is a delightful small perennial that emerges in late winter, often through snow, with bright yellow, buttercup-like flowers. These tiny gems bring a cheerful splash of color when the garden is otherwise dormant. They are best planted as corms in the fall.

Winter Cherry (Solanum pseudocapsicum), from the Solanaceae family, is native to South America. Winter cherry is a shrub known for its ornamental bright red to orange berries that resemble cherries, which persist through winter. While it does produce small, star-shaped white flowers, it's primarily grown for its striking fruit. It's important to note that the berries are toxic if ingested.

Pentas (Pentas lanceolata), from the Rubiaceae family, is native to Africa, Arabia. Pentas are tropical plants prized for their clusters of star-shaped flowers that bloom continuously. These blooms are a favorite of butterflies and hummingbirds, making them a valuable addition to pollinator gardens. They thrive in warm climates and are often grown as annuals in cooler regions.

Gazania (Gazania rigens), from the Asteraceae family, is native to South Africa. Gazanias are vibrant, daisy-like flowers that open during the day to follow the sun and close at night. They thrive in hot, dry conditions and are known for their dazzling array of colors, including rich oranges, yellows, and reds. These South African natives add a bold, cheerful presence to sunny gardens.

Osteospermum (Osteospermum), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Southern Africa. Osteospermums, often called African daisies, produce cheerful daisy-like flowers with distinctive centers. They bloom prolifically from spring through fall in a wide range of colors, adding continuous vibrancy. These hardy plants are well-suited to sunny locations and are excellent for containers and borders.

Nemophila (Nemophila menziesii), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Western North America. Nemophila, also known as baby blue eyes, is a charming wildflower native to western North America. It produces delicate, cup-shaped flowers in shades of blue with distinctive white markings. These annuals thrive in cool weather and are perfect for naturalizing in meadows or adding charm to shady spots.

California Bluebell (Phacelia campanularia), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to California, USA. The California bluebell is a vibrant native wildflower known for its intense, bell-shaped blue flowers. It adds a stunning splash of color to arid landscapes and naturalistic plantings. This easy-to-grow annual thrives in full sun and is a beautiful addition to wildflower meadows.

Monkeyflower (Mimulus), from the Phrymaceae family, is native to Americas. Monkeyflowers are known for their whimsical, open-mouthed blossoms that bear a striking resemblance to a monkey's face. These distinctive flowers come in a variety of colors, including yellows, oranges, reds, and purples. They often thrive in moist conditions and add a unique touch to gardens.

Indian Paintbrush (Castilleja), from the Orobanchaceae family, is native to North America. Indian paintbrush is a distinctive wildflower known for its vibrant, bristle-like bracts that give the appearance of being painted with red, orange, or yellow. These striking plants are hemi-parasitic, drawing nutrients from other plants. They add a bold splash of color to native landscapes and prairies.

Wild Geranium (Geranium maculatum), from the Geraniaceae family, is native to Eastern North America. Wild geranium is a charming native perennial found in woodland settings across eastern North America. It produces lovely pink to purplish flowers with delicate veining. This easy-to-grow plant thrives in partial shade and adds a natural beauty to shaded gardens.

Jack-in-the-Pulpit (Arisaema triphyllum), from the Araceae family, is native to Eastern North America. Jack-in-the-pulpit is a fascinating woodland plant with a unique hooded spathe that encloses a central spadix, resembling a pulpit. It typically emerges in spring with three to seven leaflets and a distinctive flower structure. This native plant thrives in shady, moist conditions.

Bloodroot (Sanguinaria canadensis), from the Papaveraceae family, is native to Eastern North America. Bloodroot is an early spring woodland ephemeral known for its delicate white flowers and reddish sap. It emerges soon after the snow melts, providing a beautiful, fleeting display. This native plant thrives in shady, moist woodland gardens and is appreciated for its early bloom.

Honeysuckle (Lonicera japonica), from the Caprifoliaceae family, is native to East Asia. Honeysuckle is a climbing vine known for its intoxicating fragrance, especially in the evening. Its delicate, tubular flowers are a favorite of hummingbirds and bees. The plant often sprawls beautifully over fences and trellises.

Geranium (Pelargonium hortorum), from the Geraniaceae family, is native to South Africa. Geraniums are popular, easy-to-grow plants prized for their clusters of bright flowers. They are commonly used in hanging baskets and garden beds for their continuous bloom. The plant's foliage can also have an attractive scent.

Aster (Symphyotrichum novi-belgii), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Asters are hardy perennials that bring a welcome splash of color to gardens in late summer and fall. Their daisy-like flowers, often in shades of purple, pink, and blue, are a magnet for pollinators. They are a reliable and beautiful addition to any landscape.

Orchid (Phalaenopsis amabilis), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Tropical Asia. Orchids are highly prized for their exotic and complex floral structures, making them some of the most diverse plants on Earth. Their intricate shapes and vibrant colors have captivated collectors for centuries. Many species are epiphytic, growing on other plants.

Columbine (Aquilegia vulgaris), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe. Columbine flowers are easily identified by their distinctive spurred petals, giving them a whimsical appearance. These delicate blooms attract pollinators and come in a lovely range of colors. They add a touch of enchantment to woodland gardens and borders.

Begonia Rex (Begonia rex-cultorum), from the Begoniaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Rex Begonias are grown primarily for their spectacular, intricately patterned foliage rather than their flowers. The leaves come in a dazzling array of colors, including silver, red, and deep purple, often with contrasting veins. These plants are prized for their unique, artistic beauty.

Cyclamen (Cyclamen persicum), from the Primulaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Cyclamen are charming plants known for their delicate, swept-back flowers and distinctive heart-shaped leaves. They often bloom in cool seasons, adding a splash of color indoors or in shaded outdoor areas. The intricate patterns on their foliage further enhance their appeal.

Gladiolus (Gladiolus hortulanus), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Africa, Mediterranean. Gladioli are dramatic plants known for their tall, sword-like foliage and impressive spikes of funnel-shaped flowers. They bloom in succession from the bottom up, creating a long-lasting display of vibrant colors. These striking flowers are popular for both gardens and cut arrangements.

Verbena (Verbena hybrida), from the Verbenaceae family, is native to Americas, Europe, Asia. Forsythia (Forsythia x intermedia), from the Oleaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Lupine (Lupinus polyphyllus), from the Fabaceae family, is native to North America. Lupines are striking plants known for their tall, impressive spikes of densely packed, pea-like flowers. Tiger Lily (Lilium lancifolium), from the Liliaceae family, is native to Asia.
