These charming plants bloom reliably indoors, offering shades of purple, pink, white, and blue. They are a beloved choice for bringing color indoors.

Scabiosa (Scabiosa columbaria), from the Caprifoliaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, Africa. Scabiosa, also known as Pincushion Flower, features charming, pincushion-like blooms with prominent stamens. Available in shades of purple, pink, and white, these flowers are excellent for cutting gardens due to their long vase life. They add a delicate texture and beauty to arrangements.

Sempervivum (Sempervivum tectorum), from the Crassulaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Iran. Sempervivum, commonly known as Hens and Chicks, forms tight rosettes of succulent leaves that can range in color from green to red and purple. The 'hens' produce 'chicks' (offsets) around their base, making them easy to propagate. These hardy plants are ideal for rock gardens and containers.

Senecio (Senecio cineraria), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Senecio, or Dusty Miller, is grown for its striking silvery-white foliage, which adds a unique texture and contrast to gardens. It produces clusters of small, bright yellow flowers, though the foliage is the primary ornamental feature. This plant thrives in sun and is drought-tolerant.

Silene (Silene armeria), from the Caryophyllaceae family, is native to Europe. Silene, or Catchfly, is an annual or biennial plant that produces clusters of small, bright pink to red flowers. It's often used in cottage gardens and meadows for its cheerful color. The plant adds a delicate and vibrant touch to summer displays.

Solidago (Solidago canadensis), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Solidago, commonly known as Goldenrod, is a native perennial that produces abundant plumes of bright golden-yellow flowers in late summer and fall. It is a valuable late-season nectar source for pollinators. While some varieties can be aggressive, they add vibrant color to the landscape.

Spigelia (Spigelia marilandica), from the Loganiaceae family, is native to Southeastern North America. Spigelia, or Indian Pink, is a woodland native with striking tubular red flowers that have bright yellow throats. These flowers appear in summer and are attractive to hummingbirds. It thrives in moist, shady conditions and adds a vibrant pop of color to woodland gardens.

Stachys (Stachys byzantina), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Turkey, Armenia, Iran. Stachys, commonly known as Lamb's Ears, is primarily grown for its wonderfully soft, fuzzy, silver foliage. It also produces spikes of small, purplish flowers in summer. This drought-tolerant plant is excellent for borders, groundcover, and adding texture to gardens.

Tagetes (Tagetes patula), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mexico. Tagetes, commonly known as Marigolds, are popular annuals celebrated for their bright, cheerful flowers in shades of yellow, orange, and red. They are known for their ability to deter certain garden pests, making them a beneficial addition. These plants bloom prolifically throughout the summer.

Thalictrum (Thalictrum aquilegiifolium), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Thalictrum, or Meadow Rue, is an elegant perennial with delicate, airy flower clusters that resemble fluffy plumes. These flowers, often in shades of purple, pink, or white, appear on tall stems and add a graceful, feathery texture to the garden. They thrive in moist, partial shade.

Trillium (Trillium grandiflorum), from the Melanthiaceae family, is native to North America. Trillium, or Wake Robin, is a beautiful woodland wildflower characterized by its single flower rising from a whorl of three leaves. The flowers, often white or pink, appear in spring. These protected plants are a sign of a healthy, undisturbed woodland ecosystem.

Trollius (Trollius europaeus), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Trollius, or Globeflower, is a moisture-loving perennial that produces globular, buttercup-like flowers in shades of yellow and orange. It thrives in damp meadows and along water edges. Its unique flower shape adds a whimsical touch to the garden.

Vinca (Vinca minor), from the Apocynaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa. Vinca, commonly called Periwinkle, is a popular evergreen groundcover known for its glossy leaves and charming blue or purple flowers. It spreads readily to form a dense mat, suppressing weeds and adding color to shady areas. Small white varieties are also available.

Viola (Viola tricolor), from the Violaceae family, is native to Europe. Viola, including Pansies and Violets, are small plants prized for their charming, often intricate flowers. They come in a wide array of colors and patterns, adding cheerful pops of color to gardens and containers. Many varieties have a subtle fragrance.

Yucca (Yucca filamentosa), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Southeastern North America. Yucca, or Adam's Needle, is known for its architectural, spiky foliage and dramatic spikes of creamy white, bell-shaped flowers that appear in summer. These drought-tolerant plants are well-suited for arid or sunny landscapes. The flower stalks can be quite tall and impressive.

Zauschneria (Zauschneria californica), from the Onagraceae family, is native to Western North America. Zauschneria, often called California Fuchsia, is a late-season bloomer that erupts with masses of fiery orange-red tubular flowers. These hummingbird magnets thrive in hot, dry conditions and add vibrant color to the garden when many other plants are fading. It spreads to form a colorful groundcover.

Forget-Me-Not (Myosotis), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Temperate regions. Forget-me-nots are small, charming wildflowers that produce clusters of delicate blue flowers. Their name comes from a legend about a knight who dropped his flowers into a river while drowning. These low-growing plants are perfect for naturalizing in shady or moist areas.

Hyacinth Bean (Lablab purpureus), from the Fabaceae family, is native to Africa, India. The Hyacinth Bean is a fast-growing, ornamental vine that produces attractive clusters of pea-like flowers. The most common varieties feature vibrant purple blooms, followed by decorative purple seed pods. It's a beautiful and productive plant for trellises and arbors.

Nasturtium (Tropaeolum majus), from the Tropaeolaceae family, is native to South America. Nasturtiums are cheerful, easy-to-grow annuals with distinctive round leaves and brightly colored, trumpet-shaped flowers. Both the flowers and leaves have a mild, peppery flavor, making them a popular edible garnish. They can trail or mound, adding vibrant color to gardens and containers.

Calendula (Calendula officinalis), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mediterranean region. Calendula, also known as pot marigold, features cheerful, daisy-like flowers in warm shades of orange and yellow. It is highly valued in traditional medicine for its anti-inflammatory properties and its petals can be used to add color to foods. This hardy annual is easy to grow and blooms prolifically.

Bougainvillea (Bougainvillea spectabilis), from the Nyctaginaceae family, is native to South America. Bougainvillea is a vibrant, thorny vine or shrub renowned for its dazzling display of colorful, papery bracts. These bracts, often mistaken for petals, surround small, inconspicuous white flowers and create a spectacular visual effect. It thrives in warm climates and is perfect for covering walls or trellises.

Eucalyptus (Eucalyptus), from the Myrtaceae family, is native to Australia. Eucalyptus trees are iconic for their aromatic foliage and distinctive bark, but many species also produce beautiful flowers. The blossoms are often fluffy and appear in creamy whites, pale pinks, or even reds, attracting numerous pollinators. They are a cornerstone of the Australian landscape.

Leucadendron (Leucadendron), from the Proteaceae family, is native to South Africa. Leucadendrons are evergreen shrubs valued for their colorful, long-lasting bracts rather than their small, inconspicuous flowers. These bracts, often in vibrant shades of red, yellow, or orange, form striking decorative heads. They are popular for their architectural form and cut foliage.

King Protea (Protea cynaroides), from the Proteaceae family, is native to South Africa. The King Protea is the largest and most famous species within the Protea genus, renowned for its magnificent, crown-like flower head. Its impressive size and striking appearance have made it the national flower of South Africa. The blooms are complex and visually stunning.

Bird's Nest Fern (Asplenium nidus), from the Aspleniaceae family, is native to Tropical Asia, Australia. The Bird's Nest Fern is an epiphytic fern that grows in a distinctive rosette shape, resembling a bird's nest. Its broad, glossy, dark green fronds create a lush and tropical appearance. This fern is a popular houseplant for its architectural form and ease of care.

Staghorn Fern (Platycerium), from the Polypodiaceae family, is native to Tropical regions. Staghorn ferns are striking epiphytes known for their unique, forked fronds that resemble the antlers of a stag. They typically grow attached to trees or on mounts, creating a dramatic, suspended display. Their unusual form makes them a captivating addition to any plant collection.

Maidenhair Fern (Adiantum), from the Pteridaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Maidenhair ferns are delicate and graceful, characterized by their fine, fan-shaped leaflets attached to slender, wiry black stems. This combination gives them an airy and ethereal appearance. They thrive in moist, shaded environments and require careful handling.

Rabbit's Foot Fern (Davallia fejeensis), from the Davalliaceae family, is native to Fiji. The Rabbit's Foot Fern is named for its distinctive, furry rhizomes that creep along the surface and resemble rabbit's feet. These rhizomes support delicate, lace-like fronds, creating an attractive contrast. It is often grown in hanging baskets or mounted.

Boston Fern (Nephrolepis exaltata 'Bostoniensis'), from the Nephrolepidaceae family, is native to Tropical regions. The Boston Fern is a widely popular houseplant known for its abundant, lush, arching fronds. Its dense foliage creates a classic, cascading effect, making it ideal for hanging baskets or pedestal planters. This fern prefers humid conditions and consistent moisture.

Holly Fern (Cyrtomium falcatum), from the Dryopteridaceae family, is native to East Asia. Holly Ferns are characterized by their leathery, glossy fronds that are shaped remarkably like holly leaves. This unique texture and shape give them a bold, architectural presence. They are relatively hardy and can tolerate a range of conditions.

Asparagus Fern (Asparagus setaceus), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to South Africa. Despite its name, the Asparagus Fern is not a true fern but a member of the Asparagus family. It is known for its fine, feathery, cascading foliage that creates an airy and delicate appearance. This plant is a popular choice for hanging baskets and as a filler in arrangements.

Fiddle Leaf Fig (Ficus lyrata), from the Moraceae family, is native to West Africa. The Fiddle Leaf Fig is a popular houseplant celebrated for its large, violin-shaped, dark green leaves. These dramatic leaves grow on a sturdy trunk, making the plant a striking architectural statement. It thrives in bright, indirect light and requires consistent care.

Monstera Deliciosa (Monstera deliciosa), from the Araceae family, is native to Central America. Monstera Deliciosa, often called the Swiss Cheese Plant, is famous for its large, dramatic leaves that develop characteristic splits and holes as they mature. This creates a distinctive and popular tropical look. It's a relatively easy-care plant that adds a jungle vibe to any space.

Pothos (Epipremnum aureum), from the Araceae family, is native to Southeast Asia. Pothos is a highly popular and resilient vining plant known for its heart-shaped leaves, often variegated with yellow or white. It's incredibly easy to care for and propagate, making it ideal for beginners. This plant can be grown in hanging baskets or allowed to trail along surfaces.

Snake Plant (Sansevieria trifasciata), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to West Africa. The Snake Plant is a hardy and distinctive houseplant featuring stiff, upright, sword-like leaves that are often variegated with yellow or silver. It's known for its air-purifying qualities and tolerance to neglect. This plant is an excellent choice for low-light conditions.

ZZ Plant (Zamioculcas zamiifolia), from the Araceae family, is native to East Africa. The ZZ Plant is a strikingly modern-looking plant with glossy, dark green leaves arranged on upright stems. It is renowned for its exceptional drought tolerance and ability to thrive in low-light conditions, making it a very low-maintenance choice. Its sleek appearance complements contemporary decor.

Peace Lily (Spathiphyllum), from the Araceae family, is native to South America. Peace Lilies are elegant houseplants known for their distinctive white spathes that emerge above glossy, dark green leaves. These blooms are actually modified leaves that surround the flower spikes. Peace Lilies are also appreciated for their air-purifying qualities.

Christmas Cactus (Schlumbergera bridgesii), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Brazil. The Christmas Cactus is a popular houseplant that typically blooms around the Christmas holiday season. It produces a profusion of colorful flowers, often in shades of pink, red, and white, that cascade from its segmented stems. This epiphytic cactus is relatively easy to care for.

Easter Cactus (Hatiora gaertneri), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Brazil. The Easter Cactus is another popular epiphytic cactus that blooms in the spring, typically around Easter. It features flattened stem segments and produces bright, symmetrical flowers in vibrant colors like red, pink, orange, and white. Its blooming period makes it a seasonal favorite.

Thanksgiving Cactus (Schlumbergera truncata), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Brazil. The Thanksgiving Cactus is similar to the Christmas Cactus but typically blooms a bit earlier in the season, around Thanksgiving. Its segmented stems produce abundant flowers in various colors, including pink, red, white, orange, and purple. It's a beloved holiday bloomer.

Aloe Vera (Aloe barbadensis miller), from the Asphodelaceae family, is native to Arabian Peninsula. Aloe Vera is a succulent plant famous for its medicinal gel stored within its fleshy leaves. While primarily grown for its therapeutic properties, it can produce tall spikes of tubular, usually white or pale pink flowers when mature and under optimal conditions. It thrives in bright, indirect light.

Queen of the Night (Epiphyllum oxypetalum), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Mexico, Central America. The Queen of the Night is a dramatic cactus species that produces large, intensely fragrant white flowers that open only at night. These breathtaking blooms typically last for just one night before wilting by dawn. Its ephemeral beauty makes it highly sought after.

Night-Blooming Cereus (Hylocereus undatus), from the Cactaceae family, is native to Mexico, Central and South America. Night-Blooming Cereus is a general term for various cacti that produce large, fragrant white flowers that open only at night. The blooms are often spectacular and short-lived, creating a magical nocturnal display. This phenomenon is a wonder of the plant kingdom.

Bird's Egg Orchid (Cymbidium eburneum), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to China, Vietnam. The Bird's Egg Orchid is a type of Cymbidium orchid prized for its large, waxy flowers that have a striking resemblance to speckled bird eggs. These blooms often have a beautiful, sweet fragrance. It is a visually unique and captivating orchid species.

Ghost Orchid (Dendrophylax lindenii), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Florida, Cuba. The Ghost Orchid is an incredibly rare and elusive orchid known for its ethereal, leafless growth habit and spectral white flowers. The blooms appear to float without visible foliage, creating a ghostly appearance. It is a highly protected species found in specific wetland habitats.

Vanda Orchid (Vanda), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Asia. Vanda orchids are known for their strikingly large and vibrantly colored flowers, often featuring intricate patterns and intense hues. They are epiphytic and typically grown in baskets, relying on air circulation. Their bold blooms are highly prized in the orchid world.

Dendrobium Orchid (Dendrobium), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Asia, Australia. Dendrobium orchids represent a vast and diverse genus, offering a wide array of flower shapes, sizes, and colors. Many species produce clusters of elegant, often star-shaped flowers that are highly admired. They are a significant group in orchid cultivation.

Oncidium Orchid (Oncidium), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Americas. Oncidium orchids are often referred to as 'dancing ladies' due to their abundant, small flowers that appear to be fluttering or dancing. These flowers are typically yellow or brown, often with intricate patterns. They are a popular and relatively easy-to-grow orchid group.

Tango Orchid (Oncidium 'Tango'), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Tango Orchids are a popular hybrid series known for their intensely vibrant red and orange flowers. These bold colors and the flowers' striking appearance give them a modern and dramatic aesthetic. They are a captivating choice for adding intense color.

Blue Star Fern (Arthropteris tenella), from the Davalliaceae family, is native to Australia, New Zealand. The Blue Star Fern is a charming fern with delicate, pale green fronds that often have a subtle bluish tint. Its airy texture and graceful appearance make it a lovely addition to shaded areas or as a houseplant. It prefers moist conditions and dappled light.

Laburnum (Laburnum), from the Fabaceae family, is native to Southern Europe. Laburnum, also known as golden chain trees, are famous for their dramatic spring display of long, drooping racemes of bright yellow flowers. These golden chains create a breathtaking spectacle. It's important to note that all parts of the Laburnum plant are poisonous.

Goldenrod (Solidago), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Goldenrods are native wildflowers known for their feathery plumes of bright yellow flowers that bloom in late summer and fall. They are important for supporting pollinators during this transitional period. Goldenrod provides a cheerful and essential splash of color to the landscape.

Veronica (Veronica), from the Plantaginaceae family, is native to Temperate regions. Veronicas, also known as speedwells, are charming perennials that produce spikes of small, often star-shaped flowers. They come in attractive shades of blue, purple, pink, and white, adding delicate color and texture to garden beds. Many varieties are excellent for attracting pollinators.

Azalea (Rhododendron subsection Tsutsusi), from the Ericaceae family, is native to Asia, Europe, North America. Azaleas are renowned for their breathtaking spring displays of vibrant, often massed, blooms. Originating from Asia, Europe, and North America, these shrubs are a cherished sight. Their showy flowers add a spectacular touch to landscapes and gardens.

Bougainvillea (Bougainvillea), from the Nyctaginaceae family, is native to South America. Bougainvillea is renowned for its riot of colorful, papery bracts that surround its small, insignificant flowers. Native to South America, this tropical vine thrives in warm climates and can transform fences and walls into dazzling displays. It is a popular choice for sunny, hot locations.

Cherry Blossom (Prunus serrulata), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Japan, Korea, China. Cherry blossoms are a fleeting yet breathtaking spectacle of spring. Originating from East Asia, these delicate pink or white flowers symbolize renewal and the transient nature of beauty. Their mass bloom transforms landscapes into ethereal scenes.

Dianthus (Dianthus), from the Caryophyllaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, North Africa. Dianthus, often called 'pinks', are cherished for their fringed petals and delightful, spicy fragrance. Native to Eurasia and North Africa, these charming flowers come in lovely shades of pink, red, and white. They are a classic choice for cottage gardens.

Disa (Disa), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Sub-Saharan Africa. Disas are a genus of exquisite orchids native to sub-Saharan Africa. Renowned for their complex and striking blooms, they often feature intricate petal structures and vibrant colors. These orchids are highly sought after by collectors and enthusiasts.

Evening Primrose (Oenothera), from the Onagraceae family, is native to Americas. Evening Primrose plants are fascinating as their blooms typically open in the late afternoon or evening. Native to the Americas, these flowers often release a sweet fragrance as they unfurl. They offer a unique nighttime display in the garden.

Gardenia (Gardenia jasminoides), from the Rubiaceae family, is native to Asia. Gardenias are prized for their incredibly fragrant, waxy white blossoms set against lush, glossy evergreen leaves. Native to Asia, these elegant plants thrive in warm, humid climates. Their intoxicating scent makes them a classic choice for perfumery and admired in gardens.

Geranium (Geranium), from the Geraniaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Geraniums are popular for their vibrant, saucer-shaped flowers and, in many varieties, their aromatic foliage. Found worldwide, these adaptable plants offer a wide range of colors. They are a staple in containers, borders, and hanging baskets.

Gloxinia (Sinningia speciosa), from the Gesneriaceae family, is native to Brazil. Gloxinias are cherished for their large, velvety, bell-shaped flowers adorned with intricate patterns. Native to Brazil, these tropical plants thrive indoors or in sheltered outdoor spaces. Their stunning blooms bring a touch of exotic elegance.

Jonquil (Narcissus jonquilla), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to Spain, Portugal. Jonquils are a type of narcissus prized for their sweet, rich fragrance and clusters of multiple small, bright yellow blooms. Native to Spain and Portugal, these cheerful daffodils are a delightful addition to spring gardens. Their scent is particularly intoxicating.

Larkspur (Consolida), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Mediterranean region. Larkspur offers delicate, airy spikes of flowers that add a touch of grace to garden borders. Native to the Mediterranean region, these plants are closely related to delphiniums. They are often grown as annuals and provide lovely cut flowers.

Lilac (Syringa), from the Oleaceae family, is native to Eastern Europe and Asia. Lilacs are beloved for their intensely fragrant, conical clusters of small flowers that are a sure sign of spring. Native to Eastern Europe and Asia, their sweet perfume fills the air. These shrubs are a cherished addition to gardens, symbolizing renewal.

Lunaria (Lunaria annua), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Europe. Lunaria, also known as Honesty or Money Plant, features fragrant purple or white flowers followed by distinctive silvery, translucent seed pods. Native to Europe, it is often grown for its ornamental seed heads. The plant brings a unique texture and appearance to gardens.

Mimosa (Mimosa pudica), from the Fabaceae family, is native to South America. The Mimosa plant, or Sensitive Plant, is famous for its unique reaction to touch, with leaves that fold inward. Native to South America, it also produces delicate, pink, puffball-like flowers. It's a fascinating and interactive plant for the garden or home.

Morning Glory (Ipomoea), from the Convolvulaceae family, is native to Tropical and subtropical regions. Morning Glories are vines prized for their beautiful trumpet-shaped flowers that unfurl with the morning sun. Native to tropical and subtropical regions, they come in vibrant shades of blue, purple, pink, and white. Their ephemeral blooms offer a daily spectacle.

Periwinkle (Vinca), from the Apocynaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Mediterranean region. Periwinkle is a popular groundcover known for its bright, star-shaped flowers, most commonly in shades of blue and purple. Native to Europe and the Mediterranean, it thrives in shady conditions. Its vigorous growth helps suppress weeds.

Queen Anne's Lace (Daucus carota), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Southwest Asia. Queen Anne's Lace is a wild carrot species known for its delicate, intricate, lace-like white flower clusters. Native to Europe and Southwest Asia, these blooms are a common sight in meadows and fields. It's a beautiful example of natural floral architecture.

Red Hot Poker (Kniphofia), from the Asphodelaceae family, is native to Africa. Red Hot Poker plants are dramatic with their tall spikes of tubular flowers that resemble a burning torch. Native to Africa, these striking blooms transition from red to orange and yellow. They add a bold, architectural element to gardens.

Scabiosa (Scabiosa), from the Caprifoliaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, Africa. Scabiosa, commonly called Pincushion Flower, features unique blooms with a delightful pincushion-like appearance. Native to Europe, Asia, and Africa, these charming flowers come in lovely shades of purple, pink, and white. They are excellent for cutting gardens.

Schizanthus (Schizanthus), from the Solanaceae family, is native to Chile. Schizanthus, often called the Butterfly Flower, boasts delicate blooms that resemble small orchids. Native to Chile, these plants produce a profusion of colorful flowers in shades of pink, purple, white, and yellow. They are a charming addition to hanging baskets and containers.

Snowflake (Leucojum), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa. Snowflakes are elegant bulbs with bell-shaped white flowers that resemble larger snowdrops. Native to Europe and North Africa, they often bloom slightly later than snowdrops. Their graceful, pendulous blossoms are a lovely sign of spring.

Spider Lily (Hymenocallis), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to Americas. Spider Lilies are elegant plants known for their striking white flowers with long, spidery petals. Native to the Americas, they often possess a captivating fragrance. These bulbs bring a touch of exotic beauty and fragrance to gardens.

Star of Bethlehem (Ornithogalum), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Southwest Asia. Star of Bethlehem produces delicate, star-shaped white flowers that often open fully in bright sunlight. Native to Europe and Southwest Asia, these bulbs are a charming addition to spring gardens. Their pure white blooms create a luminous effect.

Thistle (Cirsium), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Worldwide. Thistles are plants characterized by their prickly leaves and stems, crowned with striking purple or pink flower heads. Found worldwide, these plants often thrive in disturbed soils and can be surprisingly beautiful. Some species are important for pollinators.

Tuberose (Polianthes tuberosa), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Mexico. Tuberose is celebrated for its intensely fragrant, waxy white flowers, highly prized for their use in perfumes. Native to Mexico, these bulbs produce tall spikes of blooms. Their sweet, exotic scent is captivating and long-lasting.

Yarrow (Achillea), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Temperate regions of the Northern Hemisphere. Yarrow features flat-topped clusters of tiny flowers and is known for its medicinal properties. Native to temperate regions of the Northern Hemisphere, it comes in shades of yellow, white, pink, and red. This hardy plant is also attractive to beneficial insects.

Chrysanthemum (Chrysanthemum morifolium), from the Asteraceae family, is native to East Asia, Northeastern Europe. Chrysanthemums, often called 'mums', are a quintessential flower of autumn, providing vibrant color when other plants fade. They come in a vast array of shapes and sizes, from delicate pompons to large spider-like blooms. These hardy plants are cultivated worldwide for their ornamental and symbolic value.

Balsam (Impatiens balsamina), from the Balsaminaceae family, is native to Tropical Asia, Africa. Balsam is an annual plant known for its attractive, camellia-like flowers that grow directly from the leaf axils. It thrives in moist, shady conditions and is often planted in borders and containers. The plant's seed pods burst open when touched, hence its common name 'touch-me-not'.

Bellflower (Campanula), from the Campanulaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Bellflowers are a diverse group of plants known for their distinctive bell-shaped or star-shaped flowers, which often hang downwards. They come in various sizes and colors, from tiny alpine varieties to tall garden specimens. These plants are generally easy to grow and provide long-lasting blooms.

Bluestar (Amsonia tabernaemontana), from the Apocynaceae family, is native to Southeastern United States. Bluestar is an attractive native perennial that produces clusters of delicate, star-shaped blue flowers in late spring. Its airy foliage provides texture, and the fall color is a lovely golden yellow. It's a low-maintenance plant that thrives in full sun to part shade.

Browallia (Browallia americana), from the Solanaceae family, is native to Tropical Americas. Browallia, often called 'bush-violet', is an annual that produces an abundance of small, star-shaped flowers in shades of blue, white, or violet. It's a fantastic plant for containers, hanging baskets, and borders, providing continuous color from spring to frost. It prefers partial shade.

Catchfly (Silene), from the Caryophyllaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Catchfly refers to a group of plants in the genus Silene, many of which have sticky stems that can trap small insects. They produce small, often brightly colored flowers, typically in shades of pink, red, or white. These hardy plants are often found in meadows and on rocky slopes.

Celosia (Celosia argentea), from the Amaranthaceae family, is native to Tropical regions. Celosia, also known as cockscomb or woolflower, is grown for its unique, velvety flower structures. These can take the form of dramatic crested heads or feathery plumes in vibrant colors. They are popular for their long-lasting blooms and use in dried arrangements.

Chicory (Cichorium intybus), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Chicory is a wild plant known for its striking sky-blue, daisy-like flowers that typically open in the morning and close by afternoon. It has a deep taproot often used as a coffee substitute and in various culinary dishes. This hardy plant is found in fields and along roadsides.

Chionodoxa (Glory of the Snow) (Chionodoxa), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Crete, Turkey. Chionodoxa, or 'Glory of the Snow', is a genus of bulbs that bloom very early in spring, often pushing through snow. They produce star-shaped flowers in shades of blue, pink, or white. These charming little plants are perfect for naturalizing in lawns or rock gardens.

Dianthus (Pinks) (Dianthus plumarius), from the Caryophyllaceae family, is native to Europe. Dianthus, often called 'pinks', are charming plants known for their frilly-edged petals and a distinct, spicy, clove-like fragrance. They are popular for their long blooming season and attractive, often blue-green foliage. These hardy perennials are excellent for rock gardens and borders.

Fire Lily (Gloriosa superba), from the Colchicaceae family, is native to Africa, Asia. The fire lily is a spectacular climbing plant native to Africa and Asia, known for its dramatic, flame-colored flowers. The petals are often wavy and reflexed, giving them an exotic appearance. This tropical plant requires support and thrives in warm climates.

Flax (Linum perenne), from the Linaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Flax is a delicate flowering plant with slender stems topped by small, sky-blue flowers. It's known for its ornamental appeal and its historical use for linen production and linseed oil. These plants thrive in full sun and well-drained soil, often creating a hazy, ethereal effect.

Four O'Clock (Mirabilis jalapa), from the Nyctaginaceae family, is native to Tropical Americas. Four o'clocks are known for their trumpet-shaped flowers that open in the late afternoon and often release a sweet fragrance, hence their common name. They come in a wide array of colors, and sometimes different colors appear on the same plant. These plants are easy to grow and can self-seed.

Globe Thistle (Echinops), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Globe thistles are striking perennials with spherical, spiky flower heads that resemble blue or purplish thistles. They are architectural plants that add unique texture and color to the garden, especially in late summer. These drought-tolerant plants attract bees and butterflies.

Jacob's Ladder (Polemonium reptans), from the Polemoniaceae family, is native to North America. Jacob's Ladder is a charming woodland perennial recognized by its unique foliage, where leaflets are arranged in a ladder-like fashion. It produces delicate, bell-shaped blue flowers in spring. This plant prefers moist, shady conditions and adds a whimsical touch to the garden.

Lychnis (Lychnis), from the Caryophyllaceae family, is native to Eurasia, North Africa. Lychnis, commonly known as campion or Maltese Cross, features vibrant, often star-shaped flowers in bright reds, pinks, and oranges. Some species have distinctive mossy foliage. These hardy perennials add a bold splash of color to garden borders and are quite resilient.

Malcomia (Malcomia maritima), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Malcomia, commonly known as Virginia stock, is a low-growing annual with small, sweetly fragrant flowers in shades of pink, purple, and white. It blooms profusely from spring into summer and is perfect for edging, rock gardens, and containers. It's easy to grow from seed.

Mexican Hat (Ratibida columnifera), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Mexican Hat, also known as Prairie Coneflower, is a distinctive native wildflower with cone-shaped centers and drooping ray petals that resemble a sombrero. The flowers are typically yellow or reddish-brown. It's a hardy plant that attracts pollinators and thrives in dry conditions.

Nigella (Love-in-a-Mist) (Nigella damascena), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Love-in-a-mist is an annual with delicate, ethereal flowers that are surrounded by a finely divided, misty calyx. The blooms, typically blue, white, or pink, are set off by the unique foliage. It's also known for its attractive seed pods, which are used in dried arrangements.

Nolana (Nolana), from the Solanaceae family, is native to Chile, Peru. Nolana, also known as Chilean Bellflower or Alstroemeria of the Andes, is a low-growing plant producing masses of bell-shaped flowers. The blooms are often a vibrant blue or purple with a yellow throat, resembling tiny eyes. They are excellent for ground cover, hanging baskets, and rock gardens.

Onosma (Onosma), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Onosma, often called golden drop or cream broom, is a perennial with pendulous, tubular flowers that are typically yellow or cream colored. These plants often have a somewhat bushy or spreading habit and are well-suited for rock gardens and well-drained slopes. They are known for attracting bees.

Oxalis (Oxalis), from the Oxalidaceae family, is native to Worldwide. Oxalis species are recognized by their clover-like leaves, often in shades of green or purplish-bronze. They produce delicate, often five-petaled flowers in various colors, including pink, purple, white, and yellow. Some species are popular houseplants, while others are grown in gardens.

Pasqueflower (Pulsatilla), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, North America. Pasqueflowers are among the earliest wildflowers to bloom, often appearing shortly after the snow melts. They are fuzzy, bell-shaped flowers that nod gracefully on hairy stems. Following the blooms, attractive feathery seed heads develop, adding further interest.

Portulaca (Moss Rose) (Portulaca grandiflora), from the Portulacaceae family, is native to South America. Potentilla (Potentilla), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Worldwide. The blooms are often in shades of yellow or white but can also be pink or orange. Many varieties are known for their long blooming season, providing color from spring to fall.

Skimmia (Skimmia japonica), from the Rutaceae family, is native to East Asia. Skimmia is an evergreen shrub primarily grown for its fragrant clusters of small white flowers and, on female plants, its bright red berries that persist through winter. It's a shade-loving plant that adds ornamental value throughout the year. Cross-pollination is often necessary for berry production.

St. John's Wort (Hypericum), from the Hypericaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, North Africa. St. John's Wort is known for its bright yellow, star-shaped flowers that typically have numerous prominent stamens. Many species have a long history of medicinal use, particularly for treating mild depression. These hardy plants are often found in meadows and open woodlands.

This plant is relatively drought-tolerant and thrives in full sun with well-drained soil.

Its translucent 'windows' and forked 'tongues' add to its uncanny resemblance to a striking snake. This fascinating plant thrives in bogs and seepages of its native habitat.

Rafflesia (Rafflesia arnoldii), from the Rafflesiaceae family, is native to Sumatra, Borneo. Rafflesia arnoldii holds the title of the world's largest single flower, producing a massive bloom with a pungent, carrion-like smell. This parasitic plant lacks stems, leaves, and roots, obtaining nutrients from its host vine. Its immense size and unusual odor are its most distinguishing features.

Corpse Flower (Amorphophallus titanum), from the Araceae family, is native to Sumatra, Indonesia. The Corpse Flower, Amorphophallus titanum, is famous for its colossal size and its putrid odor, which attracts pollinators like flies. This giant inflorescence can take years to bloom, and when it does, it is a spectacular and pungent event. Its dark, fleshy spathe and spadix are impressive to behold.

Stapelia (Stapelia gigantea), from the Apocynaceae family, is native to Southern Africa. Stapelia gigantea, commonly known as Zulu giant, produces enormous, star-shaped flowers that mimic the scent of decaying flesh. This adaptation attracts carrion flies, which are essential for pollination. Despite their unusual smell, the flowers have a striking, intricate beauty.

Bacopa (Sutera cordata), from the Scrophulariaceae family, is native to South Africa. Bacopa is a charming trailing plant that produces a profusion of small, delicate, star-shaped flowers. It is often used in hanging baskets and containers, where its abundant blooms can spill over the edges. It prefers moist soil and partial shade.

Diascia (Diascia), from the Scrophulariaceae family, is native to South Africa. Diascia, often called twinspur, produces masses of small, unique flowers that have a characteristic twin spur. These trailing plants are excellent for containers and hanging baskets, providing a delicate and continuous display of color. They prefer cool temperatures and well-drained soil.

Bidens (Bidens ferulifolia), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mexico. Bidens is a trailing plant known for its prolific small yellow or orange daisy-like flowers. It is widely used in hanging baskets and containers, where its airy habit and constant bloom add a cheerful presence. Bidens thrives in full sun and is relatively drought-tolerant.

Eryngium (Eryngium), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, North Africa. Eryngium, or sea holly, is known for its striking, thistle-like flower heads and bracts, often in shades of electric blue or silvery white. These plants have a strong architectural presence in the garden and are very drought-tolerant. They are also excellent for drying and using in arrangements.

Symphytum (Symphytum officinale), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Europe, Western Asia. Comfrey is a vigorous perennial known for its clusters of bell-shaped flowers and its long history of medicinal use, particularly for wound healing. It thrives in moist soil and can spread readily. While valuable as a dynamic accumulator of nutrients, its internal use is now cautioned against.

Lobelia cardinalis (Lobelia cardinalis), from the Campanulaceae family, is native to North America. Cardinal flower is a stunning native perennial prized for its brilliant scarlet red flower spikes. It is a magnet for hummingbirds and thrives in moist to wet conditions in full sun to partial shade. This plant adds a dramatic splash of color to wetland gardens or pond edges.

Chelone (Chelone lyonii), from the Plantaginaceae family, is native to North America. Turtlehead is a shade-loving perennial that produces unique, hooded flowers resembling a turtle's head, typically in shades of pink or white. It blooms in late summer and fall, providing color when many other plants are fading. This plant prefers moist, well-drained soil.

Physostegia (Physostegia virginiana), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to North America. Obedient plant is a North American native perennial known for its square stems and spikes of tubular flowers that can be twisted into different positions. It blooms in late summer and fall, attracting pollinators. This plant tolerates moist soils and can spread to form colonies.

Aruncus (Aruncus dioicus), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Asia, Europe, North America. Goatsbeard is a large, clump-forming perennial that produces impressive, feathery plumes of creamy white flowers in early summer. It resembles a large astilbe and provides a graceful, shrub-like presence in the garden. Goatsbeard thrives in moist, shady to partially shaded conditions.

Kirengeshoma (Kirengeshoma palmata), from the Hydrangeaceae family, is native to Japan. Yellow wax bells is an elegant woodland perennial with maple-like leaves and delicate, nodding yellow flowers that bloom in late summer and fall. It prefers moist, shady conditions and rich, well-drained soil. This is a less common but highly rewarding plant for shaded gardens.

Polygonatum (Polygonatum), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to North America, Europe, Asia. Solomon's seal is an elegant woodland perennial with gracefully arching stems adorned with pendulous, bell-shaped white flowers. It thrives in shady, moist environments and spreads to form a beautiful ground cover. The berries that follow the flowers are often dark blue or black.

Epimedium (Epimedium), from the Berberidaceae family, is native to Asia, Mediterranean. Epimedium, commonly known as barrenwort or fairy wings, is a tough, reliable groundcover for dry shade. It produces delicate, intricate flowers, often with prominent spurs, in shades of white, pink, yellow, or red. The attractive foliage often has bronzy new growth.

Tiarella (Tiarella), from the Saxifragaceae family, is native to North America. Foamflower is a delightful woodland native with attractive, often lobed, foliage and airy spikes of foamy white or pink flowers in spring. It spreads by runners to form a lovely groundcover in shady, moist conditions. The ephemeral flowers add a delicate texture to the understory.

Anemone blanda (Anemone blanda), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Greece, Turkey. Grecian windflowers are charming spring bulbs that produce bright, daisy-like flowers in shades of blue, pink, and white. They emerge early in the season, often before many other plants have leafed out. These bulbs thrive in well-drained soil and can naturalize in sunny to partially shaded locations.

Iris reticulata (Iris reticulata), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Caucasus. Dwarf irises, such as Iris reticulata, are among the first bulbs to bloom in early spring, often appearing before the snow fully melts. They produce small but beautifully patterned and fragrant flowers in shades of purple, blue, and white. These bulbs prefer well-drained soil and full sun.

Fritillaria meleagris (Fritillaria meleagris), from the Liliaceae family, is native to Europe. The snake's head fritillary is a truly unique spring-flowering bulb, known for its distinctive nodding flowers with a checkered, bell-like pattern. They appear in meadows and damp grassy areas in its native European range. This plant thrives in moist soil and naturalizes well.

Zephyranthes (Zephyranthes), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to Americas. Rain lilies are aptly named for their tendency to bloom prolifically after significant rainfall. They produce delicate, trumpet-shaped flowers in shades of white, pink, or yellow, often appearing seemingly overnight. These bulbs are well-suited for warmer climates and can naturalize readily.

Crinum (Crinum), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to Tropics and subtropics. Crinum lilies are impressive, large-flowered bulbs that produce spectacular trumpet-shaped blooms, often fragrant, in shades of white, pink, or red. They are well-suited for warmer climates and can grow quite large over time. Crinums are a striking addition to tropical and subtropical gardens.

Agapanthus (Agapanthus), from the Amaryllidaceae family, is native to South Africa. Agapanthus, commonly known as Lily of the Nile, is a dramatic plant that produces large globes of blue or white, lily-like flowers atop tall stems. They are a spectacular sight in summer and thrive in full sun and well-drained soil. These herbaceous perennials are best suited for warmer climates or can be grown in containers and overwintered.

Eremurus (Eremurus), from the Asphodelaceae family, is native to Asia. Foxtail lilies are dramatic perennials that send up incredibly tall spikes of star-shaped flowers in late spring to early summer. They come in shades of yellow, orange, pink, and white, creating a stunning focal point in the garden. These plants require well-drained soil and full sun.

Dierama (Dierama), from the Iridaceae family, is native to South Africa. Angel's fishing rods are graceful perennials with thin, wiry stems that arch and bend, suspending delicate, bell-shaped flowers. They bloom in summer and fall, swaying gently in the breeze. Dieramas thrive in well-drained soil and full sun to partial shade.

Crocosmia (Crocosmia), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Southern Africa. Crocosmia produces upright, arching stems covered in vibrant, star-shaped flowers in shades of orange, red, and yellow. They bloom from mid to late summer, providing a fiery display of color. These cormous plants thrive in full sun and well-drained soil.

Watsonia (Watsonia), from the Iridaceae family, is native to South Africa. Watsonia, also known as bugle lilies, produce tall spikes of trumpet-shaped flowers in shades of pink, red, orange, and white. They bloom in late spring and early summer, providing a cheerful display. These cormous plants are best suited for warmer climates with well-drained soil.

Dietes (Dietes), from the Iridaceae family, is native to South Africa. African irises, or Dietes, are hardy rhizomatous perennials that produce iris-like flowers over a long season. The blooms are typically white or creamy yellow with intricate markings and last for a day or two, but new flowers appear continuously. They are very drought-tolerant and thrive in full sun.

Hesperantha (Hesperantha), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Southern Africa. Hesperantha, often called scarlet beards, is a group of cormous perennials that bloom in the fall, often opening their fragrant flowers in the evening. They produce spikes of star-shaped flowers in shades of pink, white, and red. These plants are best suited for mild climates or can be grown in containers.

Triteleia (Triteleia), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Western North America. Brodiaca, or triplet lilies, are delicate wildflowers with clusters of star-shaped flowers in shades of blue, purple, and white. They bloom in spring and early summer and are well-suited for rock gardens and naturalizing in well-drained soil. Their airy appearance adds a natural charm.

Ixia (Ixia), from the Iridaceae family, is native to South Africa. Ixia, or corn lily, produces graceful spikes of small, star-shaped flowers in a stunning array of colors, often with contrasting centers. They bloom in spring and early summer and are best grown in well-drained soil in a sunny location. These cormous plants are typically grown as annuals in cooler climates.

Chasmanthe (Chasmanthe), from the Iridaceae family, is native to South Africa. Chasmanthe produces spectacular, upright spikes of brilliant orange-red, tubular flowers that have a distinctive fan-shaped arrangement. They bloom in fall and winter in milder climates, providing vibrant color. These cormous plants thrive in full sun and well-drained soil.

Verbena (Verbena x hybrida), from the Verbenaceae family, is native to The Americas. Verbenas are known for their long blooming season and ability to thrive in heat and sun. Their clusters of small flowers create a vibrant carpet of color that attracts butterflies. These versatile plants work well in borders, containers, and hanging baskets.

Mint (Mentha spicata), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Mint is a fast-growing herb known for its refreshing scent and flavor, and its small, often purplish flowers. It readily spreads, making it ideal for containers or areas where its vigorous growth can be contained. The plant is valued for both its ornamental appeal and its versatility in the kitchen.

Borage (Borago officinalis), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Borage is a unique herb with striking, star-shaped blue flowers that have a subtle cucumber-like flavor. Both the flowers and leaves are edible and are often used in salads, drinks, and as garnishes. This fast-growing annual is a cheerful addition to the garden and a favorite of bees.

Chamomile (Matricaria recutita), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe, Western Asia. Chamomile is a fragrant herb renowned for its daisy-like white flowers with yellow centers. It's widely cultivated for its soothing properties, with the dried flowers commonly used to make calming herbal tea. This annual plant is easy to grow and self-seeds readily.

Marjoram (Origanum majorana), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Sweet marjoram is a fragrant herb closely related to oregano, known for its milder, sweeter flavor. It produces small clusters of tiny pinkish-white flowers that are attractive to pollinators. This tender perennial thrives in warm, sunny conditions and is a delightful addition to herb gardens.

Lavender Cotton (Santolina chamaecyparissus), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Lavender cotton is a fragrant subshrub prized for its finely divided, silvery foliage and small, button-like yellow flowers. It has a distinct citrusy aroma when the foliage is bruised. This drought-tolerant plant is well-suited for hot, dry conditions and is often used in borders and knot gardens.

Catmint (Nepeta x faassenii), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Catmint is a favorite for its fragrant, silvery-green foliage and abundant spikes of lavender-blue flowers that bloom for months. It's a tough, drought-tolerant plant that attracts bees and is resistant to deer and rabbits. This versatile plant is perfect for edging borders or mass planting.

Bellflower (Campanula carpatica), from the Campanulaceae family, is native to Carpathian Mountains. Bellflowers are a delightful group of plants known for their abundant, cup-shaped flowers that resemble little bells. They come in various forms, from low-growing groundcovers to taller, spiky varieties. These generally hardy perennials add soft color and charm to garden beds and borders.

Astilbe (Astilbe japonica), from the Saxifragaceae family, is native to Japan. Astilbe are valued for their beautiful, feathery plumes of flowers that add texture and color to shady garden areas. Coral Bells (Heuchera micrantha), from the Saxifragaceae family, is native to North America. Coral Bells are celebrated for their enchanting clusters of small, bell-shaped flowers that rise on slender stems above mounds of attractive foliage. The flowers are typically pale pink or white and attract hummingbirds. These versatile perennials thrive in partial shade and are ideal for borders and containers.

Lungwort (Pulmonaria officinalis), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Europe. Lungwort is an attractive woodland perennial prized for its early spring blooms and distinctive foliage, often spotted with silver. The flowers typically start pink and mature to blue, providing a beautiful color transition. It thrives in shade and moist soil, making it a lovely addition to groundcover plantings.

Fern (Matteuccia struthiopteris), from the Dryopteridaceae family, is native to Circumboreal. Ostrich Ferns are known for their large, elegant, vase-shaped fronds that create a lush, verdant feel in shady environments. These hardy ferns spread to form colonies, making them excellent for groundcover. While not typically flowering plants, their architectural form and vibrant green add significant beauty to the garden.

Daylily (Hemerocallis fulva), from the Hemerocallidaceae family, is native to Asia. Daylilies are incredibly popular and adaptable perennials, known for their trumpet-shaped flowers that typically bloom for just one day. They come in a vast array of colors and forms, making them a versatile addition to any garden. These tough plants are low-maintenance and reblooming varieties offer extended color.

Oriental Lily (Lilium 'Stargazer'), from the Liliaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Oriental lilies are renowned for their large, showy, and intensely fragrant flowers, often in shades of pink and red. These elegant bulbs produce striking blooms in mid to late summer. Their powerful perfume and dramatic appearance make them a favorite for cutting gardens and special occasions.

Asiatic Lily (Lilium x asiaticum), from the Liliaceae family, is native to Hybrid. Asiatic lilies are prized for their bright, cheerful flowers and wide range of vibrant colors, often unscented. They tend to bloom earlier in the season than Oriental lilies and are generally more robust. These lilies are excellent for adding bold splashes of color to garden beds and borders.

Gomphrena (Gomphrena globosa), from the Amaranthaceae family, is native to Tropical Americas. Gomphrena, also known as globe amaranth, features small, globe-shaped flowers with papery bracts that are exceptionally long-lasting and durable. They are a favorite for drying and preserving, maintaining their color and form. These heat-loving annuals add cheerful texture and color to gardens and arrangements.

Yarrow (Achillea millefolium 'Paprika'), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Hybrid. The 'Paprika' cultivar of yarrow offers flat-topped clusters of striking flowers that are a vibrant blend of red and yellow. This hardy perennial is drought-tolerant and attracts pollinators, making it a valuable addition to sunny gardens. The feathery foliage adds a fine texture to the landscape.

Columbine (Aquilegia chrysantha), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Southwestern North America. Golden Columbine features elegant, long-spurred flowers in a beautiful shade of golden yellow. This native species adds a touch of sunshine and unique charm to woodland or dappled shade gardens. Geum (Geum), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Geums are cheerful perennials that produce an abundance of bright, colorful flowers. Lamium (Lamium maculatum), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Spotted Deadnettle is a vigorous groundcover valued for its attractive, silvery-variegated foliage. Ajuga (Ajuga reptans), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Europe. Corydalis (Corydalis), from the Papaveraceae family, is native to Worldwide. Mertensia (Mertensia virginica), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to North America. Virginia Bluebells are an iconic spring ephemeral native to eastern North America. Calathea (Calathea), from the Marantaceae family, is native to Tropical Americas. Philodendron (Philodendron), from the Araceae family, is native to Americas. Philodendrons are popular houseplants admired for their diverse foliage shapes, ranging from heart-shaped to deeply lobed. Many species are vining, while others grow upright. They are relatively easy to care for and adapt well to indoor conditions.

Syngonium podophyllum (Syngonium podophyllum), from the Araceae family, is native to Tropical Americas. Arrowhead Plant is a popular houseplant known for its distinctively arrowhead-shaped leaves. Chlorophytum comosum (Chlorophytum comosum), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Tropical and Southern Africa. Sorbus (Sorbus), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Temperate regions of the Northern Hemisphere. Rowan, also known as Mountain Ash, is a small deciduous tree or shrub prized for its clusters of white flowers in spring, followed by vibrant clusters of red, orange, or yellow berries in the fall. These berries are a vital food source for birds. Rowans are generally hardy and adapt well to various conditions.

Asters (Symphyotrichum), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Asters are fall-blooming perennials that bring a burst of color to the garden when many other plants are winding down. Their daisy-like flowers, typically in shades of purple and pink, are a favorite of late-season pollinators. They are a hardy addition to any perennial border.

Mesembryanthemum (Mesembryanthemum crystallinum), from the Aizoaceae family, is native to South Africa. Common Ice Plant is a sprawling succulent prized for its unique, glistening surface covered in bladder-like cells that resemble frost. It produces small pink, white, or purple flowers. This plant thrives in arid, sunny conditions and is drought-tolerant.

Aster (Callistephus chinensis), from the Asteraceae family, is native to China. China Aster is a popular annual that produces an abundance of attractive, double daisy-like flowers. Available in a wide range of colors, it is an excellent choice for cutting gardens and borders. These plants bloom from mid-summer until frost.

Bracteantha (Bracteantha bracteata), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Australia. Golden Everlasting, also known as Strawflower, is an Australian native with papery, everlasting blooms that are excellent for drying. Its vibrant colors and ability to hold their shape make it a popular choice for floral crafts. The flowers come in a wide array of cheerful hues.

Gladiolus (Gladiolus x hortulanus), from the Iridaceae family, is native to Africa, Mediterranean. Gladioli are dramatic plants known for their tall, sword-like leaves and imposing spikes of large, showy flowers. Originating from Africa and the Mediterranean, these cormous perennials bloom from the bottom up, creating a stunning vertical display. They are a favorite for cutting gardens and formal arrangements.

Kangaroo Paw (Anigozanthos manglesii), from the Haemodoraceae family, is native to Australia. Kangaroo paws are iconic Australian wildflowers, instantly recognizable by their fuzzy, tubular flowers that curve upwards, resembling a kangaroo's paw. These striking plants are adapted to arid conditions and are known for their vibrant colors. They are a unique and eye-catching addition to any garden.

Lady's Slipper Orchid (Cypripedium calceolus), from the Orchidaceae family, is native to Northern Hemisphere. Lady's slipper orchids are captivating woodland plants, distinguished by their unique pouch-like petal, the labellum, which forms a 'slipper.' Found in the Northern Hemisphere, these rare and beautiful orchids are a treasure for wildflower enthusiasts. Their delicate structure and habitat preference make them particularly special.

Lychnis (Lychnis coronaria), from the Caryophyllaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Lychnis, also known as rose campion, is admired for its soft, silvery-gray foliage and vibrant, magenta-pink or white flowers. Native to the Mediterranean region, it's a striking plant that adds texture and bold color to sunny gardens. It blooms for an extended period in summer.

Mimulus (Mimulus luteus), from the Phrymaceae family, is native to South America. Mimulus, also known as monkeyflowers, are charming plants recognized by their uniquely shaped, often speckled flowers that resemble a grinning monkey's face. Native to South America, they thrive in moist conditions and add a whimsical touch to bog gardens or stream edges. They come in a variety of bright colors.

Monkshood (Aconitum napellus), from the Ranunculaceae family, is native to Europe. Monkshood is an elegant perennial known for its distinctive hooded, helmet-shaped flowers, often in deep shades of blue and purple. Native to Europe, this plant has a formidable appearance, and it's important to note that all parts are highly poisonous. It adds a dramatic, stately element to shaded gardens.

Petrea (Petrea volubilis), from the Verbenaceae family, is native to Tropical Americas. Petrea, also known as sandpaper vine, is a tropical climber celebrated for its stunning cascades of delicate, star-shaped flowers, often in shades of lavender or blue. Native to the tropical Americas, its rough leaves contrast with its graceful floral display. It brings a touch of exotic beauty to warmer climates.

Pieris (Pieris japonica), from the Ericaceae family, is native to Japan, Taiwan, China. Pieris, or andromeda, is an evergreen shrub prized for its drooping clusters of delicate, bell-shaped flowers and its attractive new foliage, which often emerges in vibrant shades of red or bronze. Native to Japan, Taiwan, and China, it prefers acidic soil and partial shade. Its spring bloom is a gentle, elegant display.

Rudbeckia (Rudbeckia fulgida), from the Asteraceae family, is native to North America. Rudbeckia, commonly known as coneflowers, are cheerful North American natives celebrated for their bright, daisy-like flowers with prominent dark centers. These hardy perennials provide reliable color throughout the summer and into fall, attracting pollinators. They are a staple of prairie and meadow gardens.

Scaevola (Scaevola aemula), from the Goodeniaceae family, is native to Australia. Scaevola, often called fan flower, is a charming annual or perennial native to Australia known for its unique fan-shaped flowers. These trailing plants produce abundant blooms, typically in shades of blue or purple, making them ideal for hanging baskets and containers. They offer a continuous display of color.

Lovage (Levisticum officinale), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Lovage is a tall, hardy perennial herb with a strong, celery-like flavor. It produces umbrella-shaped clusters of small, yellowish-green flowers in the summer. Both the leaves and seeds are edible and can be used to flavor soups, stews, and other dishes.

Angelica (Angelica archangelica), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Northern Europe, Arctic regions. Angelica is a majestic herb known for its towering stature and large, spherical clusters of greenish-white flowers. It possesses a unique, aromatic flavor with hints of anise or licorice. Traditionally, its stems and roots have been candied and used in confectionery and liqueurs.

Chervil (Anthriscus cerefolium), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Caucasus, Southern Europe. Chervil is a delicate annual herb with finely cut, fern-like leaves and small clusters of white flowers. It has a subtle, slightly sweet anise-like flavor, making it a popular addition to delicate dishes. This herb prefers cooler weather and moist soil.

Caraway (Carum carvi), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Caraway is a biennial herb recognized for its aromatic seeds, which have a distinctive earthy and slightly anise-like flavor. It produces clusters of small white or pale pink flowers. The seeds are widely used in baking, particularly in rye bread, and in various savory dishes.

Wall Rocket (Diplotaxis tenuifolia), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Wall rocket is a perennial herb with slightly peppery leaves often used in salads. It produces clusters of bright yellow, four-petaled flowers. This hardy plant thrives in sunny, well-drained locations, often found growing on walls or in rocky soil.

Laburnum (Laburnum anagyroides), from the Fabaceae family, is native to Europe. Laburnum is a small tree or large shrub that produces stunning, drooping chains of bright yellow flowers in spring. This showy display, often called 'Golden Chain tree', is a breathtaking sight when in full bloom. It prefers full sun and well-drained soil.

Acacia (Acacia dealbata), from the Fabaceae family, is native to Australia. Acacia, commonly known as Mimosa or Silver Wattle, is famed for its abundant, fluffy, bright yellow flower clusters that bloom in late winter or early spring. The flowers have a sweet, distinctive fragrance and are a valuable source of pollen for bees. This tree often has feathery, silvery foliage.

Sorbus (Sorbus aucuparia), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Sorbus, commonly known as Rowan or Mountain Ash, is a deciduous tree or shrub producing flat-topped clusters of creamy white flowers in spring. These are followed by vibrant clusters of orange-red berries that persist into winter, providing food for birds. The tree has attractive compound leaves and a rounded form.

Cotoneaster (Cotoneaster horizontalis), from the Rosaceae family, is native to China. Cotoneaster is a genus of low-growing shrubs known for their attractive foliage, small white or pink flowers, and abundant, colorful berries, often red or orange. They are excellent for groundcover, rock gardens, or cascading over walls. The berries provide a valuable food source for birds in autumn and winter.

Cherry Laurel (Prunus laurocerasus), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Southeastern Europe, Asia Minor. Cherry Laurel is a dense, evergreen shrub or small tree that produces upright spikes of small, fragrant white flowers in spring. It has glossy, dark green leaves and is often used for hedging or as a specimen plant. Be aware that all parts of the plant are toxic.

Photinia (Photinia x fraseri), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Hybrid (North America). Photinia is an evergreen shrub popular for its vibrant new foliage, which emerges in striking shades of red. In spring, it produces attractive clusters of small white flowers. It's often used as a hedging plant or a colorful accent in the landscape.

Pyracantha (Pyracantha coccinea), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Pyracantha, also known as Firethorn, is a thorny evergreen shrub renowned for its profuse clusters of white flowers in spring, followed by abundant, brightly colored berries (red, orange, or yellow) that persist into winter. It's often used for security hedging or trained against walls.

Quince (Cydonia oblonga), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Caucasus, Persia, Northern Iran. Quince is a small tree or shrub that produces beautiful, delicate pale pink or white flowers in spring. It is also cultivated for its fragrant, hard, and tart fruit, which is typically used in jams, jellies, and preserves. The fruit ripens in autumn.

Medlar (Mespilus germanica), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Southwest Asia, Southeast Europe. The Medlar is a small tree or shrub that produces unique, star-shaped white flowers in late spring. Its most distinctive feature is its fruit, which is edible only after being 'bletted' (exposed to frost and subsequent decay), giving it a soft, apple-sauce-like texture and flavor. The fruit is often tea-cup shaped.

Pear (Pyrus communis), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Asia. Pear trees are cultivated for their edible fruit, but they also offer significant ornamental value with their beautiful white spring blossoms. These blossoms appear before or with the leaves, creating a lovely display. The trees are a beautiful addition to orchards and landscapes.

Plum (Prunus domestica), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Plum trees are a source of delicious fruit, but they also provide a beautiful spectacle in spring with their abundant white blossoms. These flowers, appearing before or with the leaves, transform the landscape into a vision of delicate beauty. Plum trees are a welcome sight in any garden.

Almond (Prunus dulcis), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Middle East, North Africa. Almond trees are ornamental and productive, famous for their early spring blossoms, which can be white or soft pink. These flowers signal the coming of the edible almond nuts. The trees offer a beautiful display in early spring before their leaves emerge.

Apricot (Prunus armeniaca), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Armenia, China. Apricot trees are a delightful sight in spring, covered in delicate white and pink blossoms that signal the arrival of warmer weather. These flowers eventually give way to the delicious, fuzzy apricot fruit. The trees are cherished for both their ornamental bloom and their sweet, succulent fruit.

Nectarine (Prunus persica var. nucipersica), from the Rosaceae family, is native to China. Nectarine trees, closely related to peaches, offer similar beautiful displays of pink or white spring blossoms. These flowers are a prelude to the smooth-skinned, delicious nectarines. The trees provide both ornamental beauty in spring and delectable fruit in summer.

Raspberry (Rubus idaeus), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Europe, Northern Asia. Raspberry plants are grown for their delicious red fruit, but they also produce delicate white flowers on their canes. These flowers are a vital part of the fruit development process. The plants are often grown in rows or as hedgerows.

Blackberry (Rubus fruticosus), from the Rosaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia, North America. Blackberry plants are characterized by their thorny canes that produce white or pinkish flowers in spring and summer. These flowers are essential for developing the characteristic dark, juicy blackberries. The plants can form dense thickets and are important for wildlife.

Cranberry (Vaccinium macrocarpon), from the Ericaceae family, is native to North America. Cranberry plants are low-growing, trailing shrubs native to bogs, bearing delicate, nodding pink flowers. These flowers are essential for the development of the tart, red cranberries that are widely used in juices and sauces. They are an important crop in certain regions.

Lingonberry (Vaccinium vitis-idaea), from the Ericaceae family, is native to Arctic and Northern Hemisphere. Lingonberry is a low-growing evergreen shrub native to cool climates, producing small, bell-shaped white or pinkish flowers. These flowers develop into tart, red berries that are used in Scandinavian cuisine. The plant thrives in acidic, well-drained soil.

Huckleberry (Vaccinium parvifolium), from the Ericaceae family, is native to Western North America. Huckleberry is a shrub that produces small, usually pink or red, bell-shaped flowers, which develop into edible blue-black berries. It's native to western North America and thrives in woodland settings. The berries are similar to blueberries but often have a richer flavor.

Viburnum (Viburnum opulus), from the Viburnaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Northern Asia. Snowball Bush (Viburnum opulus 'Roseum'), from the Viburnaceae family, is native to Europe (cultivar). Red Elderberry is a shrub or small tree that produces clusters of small, creamy white flowers in spring. These are followed by bright red berries, which are generally not eaten raw but can be used in jams and jellies. It's a valuable plant for wildlife.

Passiflora (Passiflora edulis), from the Passifloraceae family, is native to Americas. Pennyroyal (Mentha pulegium), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Middle East. Echium (Echium vulgare), from the Boraginaceae family, is native to Europe, North Africa, Western Asia. Coleus (Plectranthus scutellarioides), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Southeast Asia and Australia.
