While primarily grown for its stalks and leaves, the flowering stage is a sign of its Brassica heritage.

Turnip (Brassica rapa subsp. rapa), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Europe. Turnips are root vegetables commonly grown for their edible roots. However, when allowed to grow, they produce flowering stalks bearing small white or pale yellow flowers. These blossoms are edible and belong to the mustard family.

Kohlrabi (Brassica oleracea var. gongylodes), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Northern Europe. Kohlrabi is a unique vegetable grown for its swollen, turnip-like stem. When mature, it sends up a flowering stalk adorned with small, yellow, mustard-like flowers. The flowers are edible and have a mild, slightly peppery taste, similar to broccoli rabe.

Arugula (Eruca vesicaria subsp. sativa), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Arugula, also known as rocket, is a popular peppery salad green. When allowed to bolt, it produces delicate flowers that are typically white with purple veining or pale pink. These edible blossoms add a mild peppery flavor to dishes.

Watercress (Nasturtium officinale), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Watercress is an aquatic plant known for its pungent, peppery flavor, commonly used in salads and sandwiches. It produces small, delicate white flowers arranged in clusters. This plant thrives in cool, clean running water and is a nutrient-rich addition to the diet.

Broccolini (Brassica oleracea var. italica), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Hybrid (Italy). Broccolini is a hybrid vegetable, a cross between broccoli and gai lan (Chinese broccoli). It features tender stalks and smaller florets than traditional broccoli. When it bolts, it produces small yellow flowers similar to other Brassicas.

Cauliflower (Brassica oleracea var. botrytis), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Cauliflower is a member of the cabbage family, cultivated for its dense, undeveloped flower head, called a curd. If allowed to mature or bolt, it will produce small, white, four-petaled flowers characteristic of the Brassica genus. These flowers are edible but not typically the part of the plant consumed.

Cabbage (Brassica oleracea var. capitata), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Europe. Cabbage is a leafy vegetable widely cultivated for its edible head. When cabbage plants mature and conditions are suitable, they will send up a flowering stalk producing small, yellow flowers typical of the Brassica family. These flowers are edible but not commonly eaten.

Kale (Brassica oleracea var. sabellica), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Kale is a highly nutritious leafy green vegetable known for its curly or flat leaves. When kale plants mature, they will bolt and produce clusters of bright yellow, four-petaled flowers. These edible flowers have a mild, slightly bitter taste.

Brussels Sprouts (Brassica oleracea var. gemmifera), from the Brassicaceae family, is native to Belgium. Brussels sprouts are known for the small, edible buds that grow along the stalk of the plant. Once the sprouts are harvested or the plant matures, it will produce a tall flowering stalk with small, yellow, four-petaled flowers. These flowers are edible and share the characteristic Brassica flavor.

Chard (Beta vulgaris subsp. vulgaris), from the Amaranthaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Swiss chard is a visually stunning leafy green vegetable with colorful stalks. While primarily grown for its nutritious leaves and stems, if allowed to go to seed, it will produce small, inconspicuous flowers, typically greenish-yellow. These flowers are edible but not commonly consumed.

Spinach (Spinacia oleracea), from the Amaranthaceae family, is native to Persia. Spinach is a widely consumed leafy green vegetable native to Persia. When spinach plants bolt, typically due to warm temperatures, they produce small, greenish flowers along a tall stem. These flowers are edible but generally not the primary reason for growing spinach.

Beetroot (Beta vulgaris), from the Amaranthaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Beets are root vegetables prized for their edible roots and greens. If left to mature, beet plants will produce clusters of small, greenish flowers on tall stalks. These flowers are edible but not typically harvested or eaten.

Asparagus (Asparagus officinalis), from the Asparagaceae family, is native to Europe, Western Asia, North Africa. Asparagus is a perennial vegetable grown for its tender spears. Once harvested or left to mature, the plant develops into a fern-like foliage adorned with small, delicate, bell-shaped flowers. These flowers are typically greenish-yellow and are followed by red berries on female plants.

Parsnip (Pastinaca sativa), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Eurasia. Parsnips are root vegetables with a sweet, earthy flavor, related to carrots. When mature, parsnip plants send up a tall stalk topped with large, flat-topped clusters of small, yellow flowers. These flowers are pollinator attractors and are edible.

Celery (Apium graveolens), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Mediterranean. Celery is a marshland plant grown for its edible stalks, leaves, and seeds. If left to grow, celery plants will produce flowering stalks bearing small, white flowers arranged in umbels. These flowers are edible and typical of the Apiaceae family.

Squash Blossom (Cucurbita), from the Cucurbitaceae family, is native to Americas. The flowers of squash plants, known as squash blossoms, are large, trumpet-shaped, and vibrant yellow to orange. These edible flowers are often stuffed and fried or added to dishes for a delicate flavor and beautiful presentation. They are a testament to the beauty of vegetable gardens.

Pumpkin Blossom (Cucurbita pepo), from the Cucurbitaceae family, is native to Americas. Pumpkin blossoms are large, showy flowers, typically a vibrant orange or yellow, that emerge from pumpkin vines. These edible flowers are often stuffed and cooked, offering a mild, slightly sweet flavor. Their appearance indicates that pumpkins are beginning to form.

Asiatic Lily (Lilium asiatica), from the Liliaceae family, is native to Asia. Asiatic lilies are known for their bright, upward-facing trumpet-shaped flowers that bloom in early to mid-summer. They offer a wide array of vivid colors, including yellow, orange, pink, red, and white, and are typically unscented. These hardy lilies are excellent for borders and containers.

Waldsteinia (Waldsteinia), from the Rosaceae family, is native to North America, Europe, Asia. Barren Strawberry is a low-growing groundcover that produces bright yellow, five-petaled flowers resembling those of strawberries. It forms a dense mat of trifoliate leaves, making it an effective weed suppressor. This hardy plant thrives in partial to full shade.

Azalea (Rhododendron (section Tsutsusi)), from the Ericaceae family, is native to Asia, North America, Europe. Azaleas are flowering shrubs that are a sub-section of the Rhododendron genus. Originating from Asia, North America, and Europe, they are celebrated for their profuse, vibrant, trumpet-shaped flowers. These popular plants bring a spectacular show of color to gardens in spring.

Peppermint (Mentha piperita), from the Lamiaceae family, is native to Europe, Middle East. Peppermint is a popular aromatic herb recognized for its refreshing scent and flavor. Originating from Europe and the Middle East, it produces small, purplish flower spikes. It is widely cultivated for its culinary, medicinal, and aromatic uses.

Tarragon (Artemisia dracunculus), from the Asteraceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Tarragon is an aromatic herb with a distinct anise-like flavor. Originating from Europe and Asia, it produces small, inconspicuous flowers. It is a key herb in French cuisine, particularly for sauces and chicken dishes.

Cumin (Cuminum cyminum), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Middle East, India. Cumin is an annual herbaceous plant grown for its aromatic seeds, a key spice in many cuisines. Native to the Middle East and India, it produces small white or pink flowers. Its earthy, pungent flavor is essential in dishes from around the world.

Pimpinella (Pimpinella), from the Apiaceae family, is native to Europe, Asia. Pimpinella refers to a genus of herbaceous plants in the carrot family. Found in Europe and Asia, they are known for their small white flowers. Many species within this genus are aromatic and have culinary or medicinal uses, similar to anise.

Cow Parsnip (Heracleum maximum), from the Apiaceae family, is native to North America. Cow Parsnip is a tall, robust plant characterized by its broad, compound leaves and large, flat-topped umbels of white flowers. Native to North America, it is a common sight in meadows and moist areas. Its sheer size and imposing flower heads are remarkable.

Water Hemlock (Cicuta maculata), from the Apiaceae family, is native to North America. Water Hemlock is a highly poisonous plant found in wet habitats across North America. It produces clusters of small white flowers in umbrella-like umbels, similar to many harmless plants in its family. Extreme caution is advised due to its toxicity.
